Reviving China's Economy, Japan Opposes International Cooperation, Plans to Hold Meeting in Nanjing in September, British Representative Asks Japan to Proceed Jointly, Shigemitsu Expresses Determination to Act Alone

(Nanjing) The British government has decided to send Rothschild as an economic advisor to the British Ambassador to China to investigate the issue of economic assistance to China. Clive, the British Envoy to Japan, was ordered by his government to visit Vice Minister Shigemitsu on the 8th to inform him of this matter and to request the Japanese government to cooperate with other countries in conducting a survey to restore the foundation of China's economy. Shigemitsu replied that Japan had no intention of holding a meeting with other countries to study the issue of China's economic recovery. According to a telegram from Paris, Britain and the United States intend to have Japan hold an international conference in Nanjing in September. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' view on this issue is as follows: An international conference attempting to revive China's economy proves that the countries' understanding of the Far East is the same as in the past. Under no circumstances is Japan willing to discuss China's economic problems with other countries. The direct cause of China's economic difficulties is the US silver policy. Under the control of the US President, this policy cannot reduce China's economic difficulties through international conferences. Japan has reason to oppose the international economic conference in Nanjing. Japan has already decided to assist China's economy independently, and various specific matters are underway, so there is no need to hold an international conference to discuss this issue. (United News Agency, 12th)

(London) When Britain recently proposed convening a Chinese currency conference in Nanjing, the Japanese government refused to send representatives to participate. According to London sources, Japan's refusal to send representatives was a sign of opposition to convening a currency conference. The relevant countries have finally decided to send financial representatives to China to assist the ambassadors of the countries in investigating China's currency situation. In this way, the Japanese government should not object to it, and it is said that the Japanese government has expressed its approval after the news that the British government sent Sir Ross, an advisor to the Ministry of Finance, to China as a financial representative. (Havas, 12th)

Investigation of China's Finances, French Representative Appointed, Will Come to China with British Representative in August

(London) The governments of Britain, France, the United States, Italy, and Japan previously agreed to send financial representatives to China to investigate the currency situation. The British representative has been announced as Sir Ross, an advisor to the Ministry of Finance, who will set off for China in August. The French representative is Mr. Renault, a financial deputy consul at the French Embassy in the United Kingdom, who is an expert in currency issues. He will set off at the same time as Sir Ross. In addition, the candidates for the United States, Italy, and Japan will also be announced soon. According to the speculation of financial experts who are familiar with Far Eastern affairs in this area, when representatives from various countries study China's currency issue, they will divide the country's currency into two types: domestic and foreign. Domestic currency will still be based on silver, but for foreign currency, a new method will be agreed upon. In general, the solutions proposed by representatives from various countries will be based on their own technical positions. In other words, Britain advocates that China's foreign currency be linked to the pound, France advocates that it be linked to gold, and the United States will demand that it be linked to the dollar. London financial figures have very different opinions on the issue of China's foreign currency being linked to the pound. Some express their approval, while others express their opposition. Those who oppose it believe that the addition of such a large country to the pound bloc will easily damage the position of the pound. The Scandinavian countries are also affiliated with the pound bloc, but because of their trade surpluses, the pound's market situation is often affected. This is clear evidence. (Havas, 11th)

Silver Price Rises, Manipulated by Speculators, US Treasury Secretary Replies to Senator's Letter, Already on a Healthy Progress

(Washington) Democratic Senator McCarran today released Secretary of the Treasury Morganthau's letter on the US silver purchase program, stating that the excessive rise in silver prices was caused by speculators and that these unhealthy speculative phenomena have now been eliminated, so it is already on a healthy development path. As for the Treasury Department's silver purchase situation, a total of 421,497,000 ounces were purchased in the ten months ending May 31st, which exceeded the total world silver production during the same period by 265,000,000 ounces. However, the Treasury Secretary declined to state whether the stabilization fund had sold silver. According to McCarran's letter to the Treasury Secretary, he had specifically requested this report, but the Treasury Secretary lightly brushed it aside by saying that the operation of the stabilization fund was not of general interest. The Treasury Secretary's concluding remarks were also a warning to speculators, believing that only speculators would want to question why the government did not publish the details of the stabilization fund. (National News, 11th)

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau today sent a letter to Democratic Senator McCarran regarding rumors that the United States had abandoned its silver purchase program. Silver faction senators recently appointed a five-member committee, chaired by McCarran, to meet with the Treasury Secretary to obtain his views on the Treasury's silver purchase policy. Morgenthau wrote this letter to inform them, stating briefly that the Treasury purchased a total of 421,497,000 ounces of silver in the ten months before the end of May. The excess of 265,000,000 ounces during these ten months is enough to refute the rumors that the government has stopped purchasing silver. As for why silver prices have fallen and whether the Treasury has sold silver, Morgenthau stated that, as far as he knew, the sharp rise in silver prices to 81 cents in the second half of April was not caused by ordinary legal operations in the market, but was the result of manipulation by those with special connections. The elimination of this unstable situation and force is healthy development. Morgenthau did not mention whether the stabilization fund was used to purchase silver, but stated that the purpose of the stabilization fund was related to American policy and was applied to international exchange rates, not to domestic monetary policy, so it would not be beneficial to the public to discuss the use of this fund publicly. If you think about this, you should agree with me. This is the Treasury's consistent policy since the establishment of the stabilization fund. No member of Congress or other government official has ever questioned the Treasury about the use of this fund, which shows that this situation is generally understood and is only related to silver speculation, wanting to question whether this policy is appropriate. During the above-mentioned period, the Treasury purchased 183,000,000 ounces of silver at home and abroad, paid in full, and received 25,640,000 ounces of new silver from mining, while at the same time receiving 12,850,000 ounces of confiscated silver. (Reuters, 11th)

(Washington) American Bankers Association President Huth today spoke in Omaha, opposing Treasury Secretary Morgenthau's proposal to establish a central bank. Huth stated that such an institution cannot be implemented in the United States because the US financial organization and political background are different. After its establishment, it will be used by the political party that gains power and will not benefit the business community. (National News, 11th)

(London) The Financial News commented on Hong Kong's ban on silver exports, saying, "The London financial market does not consider this to be unusual, because the sharp rise in silver prices has had a worse effect on China than on Hong Kong. Hong Kong's government's move can prevent the outflow of silver to a considerable extent, and it will also have a good effect on the Hong Kong dollar market, making the Hong Kong dollar no longer closely related to the rise and fall of silver prices. However, its effect cannot be compared with China's imposition of a balancing tax. Moreover, the Hong Kong government's move is largely a cooperative gesture towards China, because most of the silver smuggled out of China is said to pass through Hong Kong to other countries, but there is no real basis to prove this. In short, the Hong Kong government's move and the British government's sending of Sir Ross to China were announced one after another, and there must be a considerable relationship between them. It is conceivable. (Havas, 11th)

French Finance Minister Decides to Prohibit Gold Bars from Being Used as Collateral for Cash Loans, A Preliminary Step to Curb Speculation

(Paris) French Finance Minister Regnier and Bank of France President Tangrelli decided today after consultation that the Bank of France should immediately refuse to use gold bars as collateral for cash loans in order to curb speculation. However, the date of implementation has not yet been announced. It is generally believed that this move is closely related to the Bank of England's warning to London banks and major traders last week not to engage in forward gold speculation. The habit of using gold as collateral for cash loans and using it to purchase forward gold hinders the technical defense of the foreign exchange market. It is currently believed in some circles that Paris and London, or even New York, have agreed to eliminate the practice of gold speculation and the plan currently being implemented is aimed at preparing for a general understanding of exchange rates and as a preliminary step for real currency stability. (Reuters, 11th)

(Paris) Laval, the Prime Minister, discussed financial issues with Finance Minister Regnier and other colleagues today for a long time, and then met with Malvy, the Chairman of the Finance Committee of the Chamber of Deputies. The Cabinet is scheduled to meet on Thursday to conduct a comprehensive study of the financial situation and propose various solutions for discussion, but no specific measures will be determined. (Havas, 11th)

US Senate Passes Bill to Manage Public Utilities, Now Sent to the House of Representatives for Deliberation

(Washington) The Senate recently passed the bill proposed by Senators Wheeler and LeRoux by a vote of 56 to 32 and transferred it to the House of Representatives for deliberation. The bill stipulates that private companies engaged in public utilities, namely gas, electricity, water, and tram businesses, that are not beneficial to the public interest of residents, shall be dissolved after seven years. However, if a certain area constitutes an economic unit and it is necessary to gather the various public utilities under a single command organization for management, the private company shall not be dissolved. In addition, among the public utilities, those whose nature is competitive with each other, such as gas and electricity, or those that are mutually used, such as trams, can be operated by the same consortium as usual. In the future, before the liberation, it will be prohibited for them to be operated by the same consortium until the reorganization of the private companies is approved by a vote of the shareholders' meeting. Each shareholder's voting right shall be based on the number of shares, and each preferred share shall only have voting rights. Currently, public utilities are stacked on top of each other and manipulated, resulting in increased prices and damage to users, which should also be prohibited in the future. The above provisions shall be enforced by the Securities and Exchange Commission. There are many types of these private companies, and their power is also great, which has always been attacked by people in Wall Street. Now that this bill has been passed, it is tantamount to a death sentence. (Havas, 12th)

(Washington) The Senate passed the Public Utility Holding Company Bill by a vote of 56 to 32 today. The amendment proposed by the opposition to turn this bill into a common management bill and to stipulate that the government has no right to initiate litigation for the dissolution of holding companies was rejected. However, the amendment proposed by Republican Borah, stipulating that an operating company can only be governed by one holding company, was accepted by a majority of the Senate. Before the final vote on this bill, the opposition strongly criticized it. Democrat Dietrich pointed out that this bill is not a management bill but directly wants to make public utility companies subject to public control. The Senate read a letter from President Roosevelt stating that "any amendment that undermines the main purpose of this bill will be completely contrary to the claims of my address." The amendment accepted by the Senate includes a clause allowing local holding companies to control a small number of non-competing public utilities such as water. Wheeler, who was most vocal in supporting this bill, denied that the bill was unconstitutional. Borah also stated that the right to control holding companies can be implemented using interstate commerce regulations. Those in the Senate who are related to public utilities all fiercely criticized this bill. However, this bill was eventually passed by a majority, which can be seen as a major victory for the government. However, in light of the setbacks of the National Industrial Recovery Act, those who hope that the Senate will have a more generous and cautious attitude towards this bill were greatly disappointed. (Reuters, 11th)

Bolivia-Paraguay Armistice Treaty to Be Signed at 11 PM Last Night

The armistice treaty between Bolivia and Paraguay will be signed tonight at 11 pm in the capital of Argentina. Thus, the Chaco War between the two countries, which has lasted for several years and caused the loss of tens of thousands of lives, will come to an end. This is the result of mediation by the neighboring countries of Argentina, Brazil, and Chile. (Reuters, 10th)

Argentina's capital. The mediators of the peace agreement between Bolivia and Paraguay announced today with representatives of the two countries that the war between the two countries, which has sacrificed 50,000 lives in two years, can be stopped on Friday afternoon. The main points of the truce between the two countries before the official opening of the peace talks are as follows: (1) The troops of the two countries will each defend their existing positions, (2) During the truce period, a neutral committee will demarcate the boundary line, (3) The peace conference should immediately discuss the Chaco border and other important issues, (4) After the neutral committee demarcates the boundary line, the two countries' convoys must be repatriated within ninety days. (National News, 11th)

Development of Soviet Heavy and Light Industries

(Moscow) From January to May of this year, the total output of Soviet heavy industry reached 9.212 billion rubles, an increase of 25% compared to the same period last year. Gold mining increased by more than 32%, copper by 67%, lead by 99%, steel by more than 31%, pig iron by about 25%, rolled steel by 30%, wheels by more than 32%, locomotives by about 48%, freight cars by more than 135%, combine harvesters increased fivefold, tractors increased by about 20%, sulfuric acid by 32%, and acidic phosphate by more than 32%. Compared to the same period last year, coal increased by 13% and crude oil by more than 2%. In the first five months of this year, the rate of progress in most sectors of heavy industry was able to ensure the complete fulfillment of the annual plan for this year, and even exceed the plan's provisions. (TASS dispatch, 11th)

Moscow, May 17 (TASS) - Major sectors of Soviet light industry have overfulfilled their April production plans. Cotton mills produced 183,331,000 meters of cotton fabric, woolen and semi-woolen fabrics totaled 4,726,000 meters, silk fabrics totaled 2,576,000 meters, and the production of knitted goods also increased significantly. The footwear industry exceeded the production plan by 2.4%. (TASS dispatch, 11th)

British Veterans to Send Delegation to Germany, British Crown Prince Expresses Approval, German Press Sees Shift in British Public Opinion

(London) At the annual meeting of British veterans, it was decided to send two delegates to Germany to foster goodwill with German veterans. The British Crown Prince delivered a speech to the British veterans, and the newspapers unanimously praised the move. The Daily News stated that while political problems cannot be solved solely through personal contact, it is not difficult to open a convenient avenue. The Daily Mail stated that fairness and goodwill can dispel many international misunderstandings. The newspaper also sees the remarks of the British Crown Prince praising Goering and Hess as a sign of Anglo-German understanding and anticipates that the British veterans' representatives will receive a warm welcome in Germany. (National Telegram, 12th)

(London) Major-General Gort, leader of the British Legion, issued a statement to the Daily Mail regarding the delegation's visit to Germany, stating that their visit to Germany this time is unofficial and does not have any specific goals. They only hope to discuss various issues in a spirit of goodwill to promote friendship between veterans of the two countries. Therefore, the purpose of this trip is to fulfill the principle of integrating veterans of all countries recently established by the veterans. The delegation is said to be staying in Berlin for a week. (National Telegram, 12th)

(London) British veterans held their annual meeting today. The British Crown Prince attended and delivered a moving speech, strongly supporting Anglo-German understanding. He stated that he personally fully supports the association's sending representatives to visit Germany to enhance relations with German veterans. He also said that when he recently spoke with the president of the British Legion, the president proposed sending representatives to visit Germany, and he had also had this idea for some time. He believes that former soldiers who fought on the front lines are best suited to shake hands with Germans. Although they met on the battlefield in the past, the past is now history. (National Telegram, 11th)

(Berlin) The newspapers here warmly welcomed the British Crown Prince's speech at the annual meeting of British veterans promoting Anglo-German understanding. A Berlin local newspaper published an article on the front page stating that the British Crown Prince's frank speech was definitely not issued without the government's consent, so it can be seen that there has been a change in thinking on the British side. The proposals put forward by the ministers of the self-governing colonies at the time of the British Emperor's accession to the throne can especially prove this point. Veterans know that respecting the enemy is the most competent mediator to actually eliminate war hatred. The Crown Prince's speech does not lack heroic spirit, so it cannot be compared to empty talk. The spirit it embodies and the praise it has won from British soldiers are the most favorable starting point for future negotiations. The Berliner Tageblatt published a similar argument, stating that Germans have long known that various military organizations are more capable than any organization and diplomatic envoys of enhancing international relations. The visit of British veterans to Germany is especially worthy of attention because the matter was personally announced by the Crown Prince. (National Telegram, 12th)

(Berlin) The newspapers are widely publishing the speech delivered yesterday by the British Crown Prince, the Prince of Wales, at the annual meeting of the British Legion, considering it to be of great importance and discussing it. The Lokal-Anzeiger reported that "the pro-French policy adopted by the British Foreign Office is not what people in that country want to hear, nor do they want to hear a pro-German policy. What they want to hear is a purely British policy, without relying on France. We can see from the Prince of Wales's frank statement that British public opinion has changed. What the British Crown Prince said is no different from what former veterans have said, which is enough to pave the way for the smooth progress of future Anglo-German negotiations." Other newspapers compared the declaration of the British Prince of Wales with the remarks made yesterday by German Propaganda Minister Goebbels to a reporter from the British News Chronicle, with the headline "A Great Declaration on European Peace." (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Anglo-German Naval Talks to Resume on Thursday

(Paris) Today's French newspapers reported that Britain and Germany will, in principle, reach a naval agreement to serve as the basis for a future European naval treaty. Germany is reportedly prepared to compromise, agreeing to gradually implement its shipbuilding program in stages and to limit the tonnage of each warship. After the principles of this agreement are established, France will have the opportunity to speak. It is expected that a general compromise cannot be achieved in a moment, as France will have many opinions to express on what it deems necessary. However, the commentary issued by the Paris Echo differs from this. According to reports, if the Washington Naval Treaty is not re-established this year, and the United States, Britain, and Japan start a shipbuilding race, the German naval standard will naturally increase, so the 35% ratio is sufficient to resolve the problems caused by Germany's restoration of naval power. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

(London) The Anglo-German naval talks, which were suspended due to Pentecost, will resume on Thursday. At that time, Hitler's special envoy Ribbentrop and German naval experts will return to London. Ribbentrop has reported the results of the London talks to the German head of state during this holiday. It is expected that a draft agreement will be drawn up soon, containing an understanding between Britain and Germany regarding relative naval strength, namely that the German navy will be equal to 25% of the British navy. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

(London) The British government recently asked the Japanese government for its opinion on Germany's request to place warships with a tonnage of 35% of that of the British fleet. It has now received a reply from the Japanese government. According to unofficial sources, the Japanese government has no objection to Germany's request and still insists on Japan's demand for naval equality with Britain. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

(Paris) The British government recently informed the French government of the progress of the Anglo-German naval talks. This communication is currently being jointly studied by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Navy. After a decision is made at tomorrow's cabinet meeting, a response will be drafted and sent to the British government. According to well-informed sources, as a result of the Anglo-German naval talks, Britain has initially allowed the German navy to account for 35% of British tonnage. However, the British are quite concerned about how Germany will allocate this total tonnage and whether each type of warship will be built according to this ratio. Therefore, the British side is eager to learn the details of Germany's naval shipbuilding plan. The German naval representative, Ribbentrop, has now returned to Berlin and will come to London soon, presumably to provide the British government with a favorable response. It is heard that the French government is also eager to know the details of Germany's naval shipbuilding plan. According to naval countries, it is planned to hold a naval conference before the expiration of the Washington Naval Treaty. If a naval agreement is concluded with Germany, what impact will this have on the future naval conference? This is currently unknown. Moreover, if Britain, France, and Italy allow Germany to build a navy, it is tantamount to acknowledging the complete alteration of Part V of the Treaty of Versailles, which is also a difficult problem. Not only that, but some believe that naval negotiations with Germany must be held simultaneously with the various talks stipulated in the London Declaration of February 3. If other security conventions are not discussed, the German naval issue cannot be finally resolved. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Preparations for Wenzhou Paper Mill

(Nanjing) Mr. Liu Weichi, along with British consultant Stuart Watt, experts Yang Zongmi and Jin Han, etc., went to Wenzhou at the end of last month to survey the site for the paper mill. After returning to Nanjing, it was reported that preparations for the paper mill have been going on for more than a year and the plan has long been finalized. More than 4 million yuan in official shares have been approved by the Boxer Indemnity Fund Association, but it is difficult to allocate them at once. Mr. Wang Yunwu and others are trying to raise 1.2 million in commercial shares. Mr. Liu's opinion is that Wenzhou is suitable as the factory site, as there are no problems with transportation and raw materials. However, it is still difficult to solve the electricity generation problem, whether to use water power or coal. Although burning coal saves on opening expenses, the costs are significant. Water power requires redundant construction of active dams and machinery and equipment, which is very expensive. The decision on which to use will be decided at the official and commercial shareholders' meeting. Regarding the output of paper, it is planned to produce 35 tons of newsprint per day, about 10,000 tons per year, which is not enough to supply the Shanghai newspapers. Production will be increased later to ensure that newspapers across the country can purchase it. However, it is not yet possible to talk about the output of paper materials. (Special dispatch, 12th)

Abundant Wheat Harvest in the Xuzhou Region, Average Yield Approximately Seven to Eight Dou Per Mu; Banks Launch Rural Loan Programs

Xuzhou Correspondence: The provinces of northern Jiangsu, Henan, Anhui, and Shandong were originally wheat-producing areas. In recent years, they have frequently suffered from floods and droughts, resulting in poor harvests. Farmers have struggled to afford food and clothing, and starvation has been a concern. This year's wheat harvest is now nearing completion. According to surveys of wheat harvests in the Xuzhou region, with the exception of the three counties of Sui, Pi, and Su, which suffered from sudden wind and hail damage when the wheat was setting, the remaining counties of Tong, Xiao, Feng, Pei, Dang, and Huaihai have all reported abundant harvests. The average yield is approximately seven to eight dou per mu. When new wheat is brought to market, the selling price is around five jiao per dou. Farmers typically sell their new wheat to repay debts and purchase clothing, but the market price of new wheat is extremely low, forcing them to sell against their will. Last year, new wheat sold for only three jiao per dou, while rice prices soared to six jiao per dou in one month. As a result, merchants who purchased new wheat earned more than half their profits in one month. This year, the banking sector has recognized that loans to urban industries and businesses have often resulted in bankruptcies and losses. In recent years, most bank failures have been due to the woes of commercial merchants. Therefore, this year, in addition to conducting secured loans, banks have completely overturned all credit loans, and merchant credit has plummeted. Although the Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly attempted to persuade banks to provide loans, all banks have refused. Furthermore, due to the fact that Farmers' Banks have been investing in rural areas for many years, specializing in mortgage grain loans, enjoying good credit, and receiving full repayment of principal and interest on schedule, with substantial profits, various banks are following the example of Farmers' Banks and changing their business strategies by investing in rural areas. Recently, in addition to the Jiangsu Farmers' Bank's rural loan program, other banks such as the National Bank, the Shanghai Bank, and the China Farmers' Bank are actively establishing warehouses and providing guidance for cooperation in the counties of Xuzhou this year, specializing in farmers' storage and mortgage of grain in exchange for cash loans. When grain prices rise next spring, they will then deliver the grain to farmers for sale, paying both principal and interest. Banks also handle transportation and sales matters, enabling agricultural products to connect with other ports, increasing commodity prices, and preventing low grain prices from harming farmers. Therefore, this year, the wheat harvest in northern Jiangsu is abundant, and farmers are cheering for a bumper year. With the mortgage loans from banks, they will not have to sell new wheat against their will, and rural economies will be able to regulate and adjust. The future of urban industries and businesses should be able to move toward a similar prosperous situation.

Page 8

Panic Over Food Supply Worsening in Counties Under Puppet Organizations Due to Ban on Planting Sorghum and Shortage of Grain; Puppet Provinces and Counties All Prohibit Grain from Leaving Their Borders

Shenyang Correspondence: In the four northeastern provinces, due to the puppet organizations' prohibition on planting sorghum, in order to prevent the hiding of righteous armies, only crops such as wheat that are not particularly tall and dense are permitted to be planted. Furthermore, the harvest was poor last year, resulting in an extreme shortage of grain this year. Grain prices have soared, and the food problem in various counties and villages has become critical. The people are hungry and resentful, and their voices reach the sky. Currently, the puppet Fengtian Provincial authorities have issued orders prohibiting grain from leaving the province and ordering all counties to prohibit grain from leaving the county, demonstrating the severity of their grain panic. The food panic situation in the various counties of the puppet province is described below:

Zhangwu County: The harvest was poor last year, and there has been an unusual drought since the spring and summer of this year. Grain prices have skyrocketed. Currently, one dou of sorghum is priced at a staggering two yuan and seventy-eight jiao. The number of unemployed farmers is increasing daily, and many have joined the righteous army because they have no way to make a living (this is why the Northeast Righteous Army has been very active recently). Although village chiefs have established food relief maintenance associations to investigate grain reserves, and the puppet county magistrate has prohibited grain from leaving the county, this has only caused panic.

Qingyuan County: The puppet county government investigated grain reserves within the county and determined that they were severely insufficient. It then issued a puppet order instructing distilleries under its jurisdiction to stop brewing alcohol.

Fushun County: The county's civilian grain supply has historically been mostly supplied by the eastern border region. Since the spring of this year, grain shipments have been extremely scarce, forcing them to rely on other counties. However, grain prices are extremely high, and all counties prohibit grain from leaving their borders. The county's lack of civilian food has reached an extreme point. The people are restless and there is a tendency for civil unrest. The puppet authorities are deeply frightened and are urgently formulating countermeasures.

Xinmin County: The county produces slightly more grain than other counties, so the famine situation is not as serious. However, the puppet county authorities are still ordering that grain not leave the county in order to prevent a major famine from occurring in the future.

Yi County: The puppet county authorities issued a puppet order to maintain civilian food supplies, prohibiting the export of grains such as sorghum, millet, buckwheat, and other grains.

Suizhong County: The county currently has a grain reserve of over 11,700 shi, while the public's need for grain is over 47,800 shi, leaving a shortfall of over 36,100 shi. Furthermore, the continuous drought has eliminated any hope of a harvest from spring plowing, and grain prices are rising daily, causing the people to become increasingly fearful. The county is now in a state of confusion.

Heishan County: Although the Heishan puppet county authorities have issued official documents prohibiting the export of grain, this has not been effectively implemented, and the storage is extremely small. The general public feels a great fear of a lack of food.

Chaoyang County: The Chaoyang puppet county authorities have not yet issued a prohibition on the export of grains or other concrete remedial measures, so the public is extremely apprehensive.

Xi'an County: The Xi'an puppet county authorities have issued a puppet order prohibiting the export of grain, but the actual situation is the opposite. In early May, there was still 10,000 shi of accumulated sorghum, but by early June, it had decreased by 6,000 shi, so the public's food supply is also severely inadequate. (Northeast News Agency)

Shang Zhen Assumes Office as the Tianjin Garrison Commander and Acting Mayor

Tianjin Correspondence: The newly appointed Tianjin Garrison Commander and Acting Mayor Shang Zhen arrived in Tianjin on the evening of the 8th. On the morning of the 9th, he went to the municipal government on Hebei-Japan Latitude Road to assume his position as the acting mayor. The municipal government received the news beforehand and made arrangements overnight. Former Mayor Zhang Ting'e personally went to the municipal government to hand over the seal of office. Mr. Shang arrived at the municipal government at 8:10 AM. After a brief rest, he held a simple ceremony in the municipal government's auditorium. More than a hundred people, including the directors of various bureaus under the municipality and all the staff of the municipal government, participated. After performing the formalities, Zhang Ting'e handed over the seal of office. After receiving the seal, Mr. Shang addressed all the staff, briefly saying that he had received an order from the Executive Yuan to temporarily act as the mayor of Tianjin because Mayor Wang Shu'lu had not yet arrived in the north. Many of the colleagues here are old friends, and the previous mayor achieved excellent results during his tenure. He is only serving temporarily and did not bring anyone with him, so he would not change any of the current personnel. He hoped that everyone would consider the three aspects of the country, the local area, and personal friendship and work hard to help. Next, Zhang Ting'e delivered a farewell speech to the staff, saying that he had made no achievements in the past and that he greatly admired Mr. Shang's spirit in coming to take office and bear the heavy burden during this serious diplomatic period. After finishing his speech, Mr. Zhang left the government and returned to his residence. Mr. Shang then summoned the directors of various bureaus under the municipality to inquire about the municipal situation and met with the press to make a statement, saying that his coming here was of a temporary nature and that he hoped everyone would help him from time to time. Mr. Shang then went to the former site of the provincial government to assume the position of Tianjin Garrison Commander. However, as everything in the Garrison Command Headquarters was still waiting to be arranged, no ceremony was held. He officially began working that day. Furthermore, Municipal Government Secretary-General Wang Yu'ke had previously requested to resign. After being approved by Acting Mayor Shang, he appointed Mr. Wang Bingzhe, the Deputy Chairman of the Municipal Government Statistics Committee, to serve concurrently on a temporary basis. Moreover, after assuming the position of mayor, Shang Zhen issued an inaugural telegram, the original text of which is as follows: (Omitted titles) Everyone is aware that I received a telegram from the Executive Yuan on the seventh of the solar month, stating that before Tianjin Mayor Wang Ke'min arrives, Tianjin Garrison Commander Shang Zhen should temporarily serve as the Mayor of Tianjin, etc. On June 9th, I received the seal of office and began my duties. In addition to sending separate telegrams and letters, I am sending this special telegram for your information. Tianjin Mayor Shang Zhen respectfully greets you (9th) Seal. After the provincial capital was relocated, Tianjin Municipality was changed to be directly under the Executive Yuan. The Public Security Bureau was restored to municipal control. The new Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau will be Liu Yushu, the Secretary-General appointed by the Pingjin Military Branch. Liu arrived in Tianjin at 11:45 AM on the morning of the 9th and is scheduled to go to the bureau at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 10th to begin his duties. The furniture of the former Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau will be handed over by Li Junxiang. According to Mr. Li's statement to reporters, the Provincial Government's Public Security Bureau should have been closed after the provincial government was relocated. However, because no one was responsible for the local area, he temporarily maintained it. Now that Commander Shang has arrived in Tianjin and the new Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Liu Yushu, is also preparing to take office, he will hand over the furniture of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau after meeting with him and then submit it to the provincial government and the municipal government for supplementary procedures. After completing the handover, he will temporarily stay in Tianjin to handle the matter of the changing of guards for the 51st Army. After this matter is completed, he will return to serve in the headquarters of the 51st Army. (10th)

Resolution of the Shandong University Compensation Issue; Han Fu'qu and the Japanese Consul Consulted with Labor and Management and Decided to Give 330 Yuan to Each Family of the Deceased; The Relief Committee Resolved to Erect a Monument and a Public Cemetery

Jinan Correspondence: Han Fu'qu departed from Jinan on the evening of the 9th. The special train stopped at the Zaoyuan Temple Station that night and departed at 4:00 AM on the morning of the 10th, arriving at Zhoucun at 5:10 AM. The commander of the 22nd Division, Gu Liangmin, led the division staff and a company of pistol-wielding soldiers to welcome him at the station. Wu Liansheng, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, also led all the police officers and gentry and merchants. After Han exchanged greetings with the welcomers, he practiced martial arts with his advisors, Guo Zhigang and Ge Jinzhang, as well as the Tongzi Performance Troupe of the National Arts Hall, which was selected to participate in the National Arts City Examination in Qingdao, Yang Guanghan, and others on the train. At 6:00 AM, Han went to the Jindehui to participate in the commemorative weekly meeting and lectured to the students of the garrison troops, the police officers of the Public Security Bureau, the Bureau of Tobacco and Alcohol Taxes, the Bureau of Industry, and the public, speaking on the meaning of Jindehui. At 7:30 AM, he returned to the station for breakfast. The train departed at 9:00 AM and arrived at Zhangdian at 9:30 AM. Ning Chunxiao, the commander of the 64th Brigade, led the troops to welcome him at the station. Han immediately ordered Ning to invite Gao Heng, the special director of Shandong University in Qingdao, and Shiyoshi, the Japanese special director, to Zhangdian to discuss the Shandong University aftermath. The Japanese consul stationed in Zhangdian and the Japanese consul stationed in Jinan, Nishida, also rushed from Jinan. They strongly invited Han to visit Zichuan. At 10:30 AM, Han and Nishida and Ning Chunxiao left Zhangdian by special train and arrived in Zichuan at 11:00 AM. Zhang Yunzao, the county magistrate, Wang Guojun, the director of the Public Security Bureau, and all civil servants, as well as Gu Chi and other standing committee members of the Dinghui, all welcomed him at the station. Che Tian Zichuan was reopened to the Shan mining area, and Zhang Yunzao, Gu Chi, and others also traveled on the same train. At 11:50 AM, Han arrived after getting off the train. The Shandong University company hosted them at the club for a rest. Han then invited Japanese Consul Nishida and important Chinese and Japanese personnel from Shandong University to discuss the aftermath. Regarding the compensation for the deceased workers, Shandong University only agreed to give 302 yuan per person according to custom, plus 10 yuan for the outer coffin, for a total of 312 yuan. The families of the deceased demanded a special compensation of 500 yuan per person because Shandong University could not drain the water to retrieve the bodies, but Shandong University did not agree. Although the aftermath committee had been established for many days, there was no solution due to the large differences in opinions between labor and management. Since Ning Chunxiao arrived in Hongshan on the 9th and proposed a compromise solution, requesting Shandong University to allocate an additional 40,000 yuan for compensation, Shandong University still did not agree. Song Biru then went to Qingdao to negotiate with the Shandong University management, but no progress was made. Therefore, after Han arrived, he first discussed this point with the Shandong University company. As a result, Shandong University agreed to give 330 yuan to each family of the deceased worker to show preferential compensation. Han himself also donated 540 yuan, giving one yuan to each family of the deceased worker. Thus, the compensation issue was resolved. At 1:00 PM, Han went to inspect the accident mine shaft and then went to the West Mountain and Liangshui Pond with Japanese Consul Nishida. At 2:00 PM, they returned to the Shandong University office together. Five or six hundred family members of the deceased workers, hearing that Han had arrived in the mining area, asked to see him. Han agreed to meet them at the Shandong University Elementary School at 5:00 PM. At that time, the family members of the deceased workers gathered in the elementary school. Japanese Consul Nishida, Brigade Commander Ning Chunxiao, County Magistrate Zhang Yunzao, Union Chairman Gu Chi, and others accompanied Han. Han spoke, first expressing his condolences, then introducing Nishida to speak, who also added his condolences. Han then gave a long speech and announced the compensation method of Shandong University, asking those who agreed to raise their hands. Everyone raised their hands. He also said that all those who agreed should stand on the east side of the field. As a result, everyone went to stand on the east side of the field, with only two or three people not going. Han, believing that everyone had agreed, instructed County Magistrate Zhang Yunzao and Brigade Commander Ning Chunxiao to handle the matter properly and to have the funds withdrawn and distributed to the families of the deceased by the union. At 6:30 PM, Han returned to the club. Gao Heng, the special director of the Shandong University company, Fujii, the business director, and Song Biru and others arrived from Qingdao by Jiaoji Railway to visit Han and express their gratitude for resolving the aftermath. Han urged Shandong University to resume work and asked in detail about opening new wells and draining old wells. At 10:00 PM, Han left Shan and went to Zichuan for the night. The next morning, on the 11th, he went to Yidu for inspection.

Now that the Shandong University company's compensation issue has been resolved, the Aftermath Committee held its second formal meeting on the 11th, passing six compensation methods and resolving to erect a memorial monument and establish a public cemetery, as well as hold a memorial service. The methods passed at the meeting are recorded below: A. Shandong University Company, Zichuan Mining Office, Ten Line Deceased Workers Compensation Method: After investigating the water disaster that occurred at Ten Line this time, which was an unprecedented disaster for the company, the rescue situation has been understood by all parties. From the current situation, it is not easy to retrieve the bodies. If they are retrieved in the future, it may be difficult to identify them, delaying the time and causing disputes. To avoid disputes, this committee has formulated six specific methods, listed one by one below for compliance: (1) This time, there are ten deceased inner-mine workers and 526 outer-mine workers, to be handled according to the company's usual compensation methods. (2) Because the bodies of the deceased workers are not easy to retrieve this time, the company expresses its apologies and gives 28 yuan to each family of the deceased to cover living expenses. Regardless of whether the bodies are retrieved in the future, no further demands shall be made. (3) The compensation for inner-mine workers will be paid directly by the company. The compensation for outer-mine workers will be handed over by the company to the county government for distribution in full. The detailed methods will be determined separately by this committee. (4) The company will hold a memorial service on a regular basis and notify all families of the deceased to participate at will. (5) Regardless of whether the bodies of the deceased workers are retrieved this time, the company will first select a suitable location to erect a memorial monument and engrave the names of the deceased workers one by one to commemorate them. However, when the bodies can be retrieved in the future, the company will establish a public cemetery in the location of the memorial monument for joint burial. (6) This method will be implemented after being passed by the committee. B. Regarding how the detailed methods for the distribution of compensation should be determined, please make a public decision. It was decided to hand it over to the county government, the Shandong University company, the Zibo union, and the local community to discuss and handle jointly, and to begin distribution on the 13th. The motion was read out, and the meeting adjourned. The minutes were handed over to the county government for preservation. (11th)

Qingdao Municipal Government Consults with the Ministry of Finance to Rescue Various Industries; Adopt Recommendations of the Economic Discussion Conference and Allocate Large Sums to Rescue the Business Community

Qingdao Correspondence: Since the collapse of Minghua Bank in Qingdao, the financial community has formed an unprecedentedly serious situation. Credit has tightened sharply, people are panicked, and various industries are feeling uneasy. The Qingdao Economic Discussion Conference, in order to quickly seek maintenance, specially proposed a suggestion from the financial group, requesting the municipal government to petition the central government to order the financial industry to allocate large sums of money to rescue Qingdao's industry and commerce. The original text of the suggestion stated, "The establishment of this conference to study economic matters should be based on factual investigations, formulate plans, and gradually implement them to promote the development of the city's industry and commerce and the prosperity of the market is a fundamental solution. However, this city is suffering from the impact of the global economic downturn, and industry and commerce have declined to an extreme point. At present, there are hundreds of large and small stores that cannot maintain their operations and are urgently awaiting closure, reporting to the Chamber of Commerce. If special methods are not established to rescue them, then the city's entire market will decline further and further, and the consequences will be unimaginable. Reports say that the central government has ordered the financial industry to raise 20 million yuan for Shanghai to lend to various industries to provide rescue. The environment of this city is no less than that of Shanghai, and the total amount of annual income collected by the Qingdao Customs accounts for the third largest in the country. In order to maintain the port with more tariff income, the central government should not allow this city to become paralyzed. It is proposed that the conference suggest to the municipal government to petition the central government to order the financial headquarters to allocate several million yuan to this city to be lent to the city's endangered industries and businesses in order to salvage them. This is a short-term emergency plan to rescue the city's market. Is it feasible? Your public decision is respectfully awaited." The municipal government, based on the presentation, recognized that the various sections presented by the conference were extremely important and immediately consulted with the Ministry of Finance, writing, "According to the presentation of this city's Economic Discussion Conference (original text omitted) and other circumstances, after investigation, the matter of rescuing this city's industry and commerce, the City Chamber of Commerce previously presented a request to transfer and earnestly request your Honorable Mayor to approve and provide rescue according to the rescue methods of Shanghai's industry and commerce. At that time, the situation of various industries here was indeed extremely critical, so on April 30th, we consulted you for review and handling. Now, the situation is turbulent and even more precarious. The Bank of China and Russia experienced runs, and this government worked with the Banking Association to maintain the situation with great effort, barely stabilizing it. However, before even ten days had passed, Minghua Bank also announced its collapse. In such a small area, runs, withdrawals, and bankruptcies have occurred one after another within more than ten days. Rumors have spread, and the market is tense in an unprecedented way. People are panicking and cannot live in peace. If the situation is allowed to develop, industry, commerce, and finance will all perish together, and it is feared that the impact will affect all parts of the country. To overcome this situation of doubt and turbulence, there is no other solution than to raise a large sum of money for real rescue. The conference's request to order financial institutions to allocate funds to be lent to this city's industry and commerce is indeed the only way to solve the current crisis. I once again earnestly appeal to Your Excellency the Minister to approve the request and kindly grant a quick review and reply to strengthen public friendship." (June 10th)

Han Zishi and Others Petition for the Urgent Opening of the Lake Ports for Relief Transportation; Chairman Chen Has Telegraphed Director Shen to Comply

Zhenjiang News: Since the beginning of summer, there has been no rain in the counties north of the Jiangsu River in Jiangsu Province, and a drought has appeared. The gentry Han Zishi and others yesterday specially telegraphed Provincial Chairman Chen Guofu and Construction Director Shen Baixian, requesting that the ports be opened in a timely manner for relief transportation in order to provide relief. It is heard that Chairman Chen has approved the request and telegraphed Director Shen, who is inspecting river works in Huaiyin, to comply with the order immediately. The original telegram from Han and others is recorded below: "The water in the canal has dried up, and a drought has appeared. Late rice is waiting to be transplanted, and early seedlings are about to wither. The rural areas are in dire straits. After the floods in northern Jiangsu, how can they withstand another drought? It has been investigated that the lake water at the Jiusheng Port and Qilizha in Gaobao and other places is one to two feet higher than the canal water. However, after the western embankment was dammed, lake transport was blocked, and irrigation was impossible. It seems appropriate to open the ports in a timely manner for relief transportation, which is more convenient than any other method. Blocking them again afterwards will not hinder the guidance of the Huai River project, and the cost in the future will also be less, while the gains at this time will be great. Farmers take the fields as their lives, and the lives and properties of tens of counties in the east are enormous and of great importance. If the situation is not remedied early, if an incident occurs, there will be special responsibility. Director Shen of Construction is currently inspecting the works in northern Huai, and it is requested that Director Shen be telegraphed to quickly select ports to open and save lives. I think the Chairman cares about the people's suffering and will be able to weigh the pros and cons and make a decisive decision, lest it be too late. Urgent awaiting orders."

Salt and Kerosene in Jiangxi Province Operated by Cooperatives to Avoid Exploitation and Manipulation by Merchants; The Military Headquarters Orders the Provincial Government to Transfer the Order to Various Counties for Compliance

Nanchang Correspondence: Commander-in-Chief Chiang, in order to eliminate banditry, has specially sealed off the bandit areas, and salt, kerosene, and daily necessities are all subject to control, so that not even a drop can leak into the hands of the bandits. At present, the Red Bandits in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian have been gradually suppressed, and the counties where the scattered bandits have been eliminated and the Baojia system has been completed will have the blockade lifted in order to restore normalcy and free circulation. However, the phased lifting of the blockade issued by the Military Headquarters stipulated that after the abolition of the public sale of salt and kerosene, they should be handed over to the joint cooperatives of the respective counties for centralized operation, which can establish the foundation of a controlled economy, reduce the manipulation and exploitation of intermediaries, and promote the development of cooperative undertakings. Original oil and salt traders will also be accommodated if they can invest, so as to avoid their unemployment. It is heard that the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang have successively centralized the operation of oil and salt in cooperatives. (6th, 7th)

Songjiang: Using Baojia System to Eradicate Locusts

The eighth district of the county, bordering the coast, has suffered from severe crop failures in recent years due to drought. Recently, locusts were discovered in Chongque Township in the district. Lu Chunrong, the township leader and Baojia chief, reported this to Wu Changding, the district head, who recognized the seriousness of the situation and telegraphed the county government, requesting that technician Chen Xingyuan from the Rice Crop Experiment Field be sent to investigate. At the same time, the district head and Xu Anshi, the township head, were instructed to listen to technician Chen's guidance and to diligently carry out the work. Technician Chen then returned to Songjiang and reported that the initially discovered locust-infested area was only a dozen acres. Xu Qingchang, the township head, supervised the Baojia chiefs in using tools and purchasing several cans of kerosene to cut down and burn the surrounding reeds to eradicate the locusts. Recently, however, the locust-infested area has been found to have reached over a hundred acres. If measures are not taken to search and destroy them, it is feared that it will cause great harm. County Magistrate Jin decided to take this opportunity to test the Baojia system. He ordered District Head Wu to mobilize all township, Baojia, and household chiefs. At the same time, he ordered thirty men from the security brigade stationed in Shanyang, as well as the chiefs of the nine branch police stations, to start searching and capturing locusts at 9:00 a.m. on the 11th. County Magistrate Jin and Director of Public Security He set off by car at 7:00 a.m. on the 11th and arrived at the location. District Head Wu had already led his subordinates to wait, along with the heads of the three townships of Zhalin, Huqiao, and Caojing, as well as elementary school teachers and staff, totaling about 1,400 to 1,500 people. According to the plan set by technician Chen, the area surrounding the locust-infested area was cleared to prevent them from escaping. Then, vertical and horizontal roads were opened up in the district, and the area was divided into sections, each assigned to a Baojia chief to supervise the household chiefs in cutting grass and using tools to eradicate the locusts. The county government bought the locusts for 160 cash per pound. From morning to night, more than a thousand pounds were collected. The grass was cleared, and more than half of the locusts were eliminated, so they should not spread. Before leaving, County Magistrate Jin ordered District Head Wu and others to continue eradicating the locusts yesterday and scheduled to return to the countryside on the 13th to inspect for any remaining locusts. At the same time, locusts were also discovered in more than a dozen acres in Niangniangmiao Township in the district. Township Head Lu was ordered to use the Baojia system to eradicate them simultaneously yesterday. It is said that they were almost completely searched and captured within four hours. County Magistrate Jin led his subordinates to inspect in person and praised them greatly. County Magistrate Jin returned to Songjiang and told people that this locust eradication was greatly benefited from the Baojia system; otherwise, it would not have been so swift and effective.

Suzhou: Husband Stabs Wife and Daughter-in-Law with Knife

Lu Gao, 52 years old, lives at No. 1 Qigan Lane, Huxiangsi Lane, in this city. Her husband, Lu Xiaodi, does not engage in honest work and has been separated from Lu Gao for more than twenty years. Her son, Gao Weilin, is in his twenties and works at Mao Hai Foreign Firm in Shanghai. He is married to a Chen woman and has a son and a daughter. Weilin lives with his mother. Recently, Lu Xiaodi learned that his son was working at a foreign firm, so he returned home, and his wife could not refuse him. However, Lu Xiaodi relapsed into his old habits, making excessive demands of his wife and son. His wife refused, so Lu Xiaodi harbored resentment. At 7:00 p.m. on the 11th, he took a kitchen knife and slashed his wife, Lu, and then slashed his daughter-in-law and granddaughter. The three injured people all collapsed to the ground in pain, lying in pools of blood. Lu Xiaodi, seeing that he had caused trouble, immediately fled. Neighbors heard the cries for help and rushed to see what had happened. After learning the details, they reported to the police precinct in charge and sent the injured people to Boxi Hospital for treatment. Because they were not critically injured, their lives were not in danger. The police precinct in charge immediately dispatched police to arrest the murderer, but his whereabouts are unknown.

Changshu: Exhumation After Brother is Buried Alive

Xu Heshang from Dongqian Township, Ouchi Town, killed his biological brother, Tan Songsong, and buried him alive in the Luojia Duan Mulberry Field. On the 10th, someone discovered this and reported it to the county. Xu Heshang, the murderer, was arrested. The case caused a sensation and drew great attention from society. According to the confession, his brother had a wandering nature and repeatedly asked for money. On the 6th, they had a mutual fight in the Shi Surname Hotel. The next day, he vomited and died in the afternoon. Fearing accusations, he buried him in the field without a coffin, but he did not admit to killing him. On the afternoon of the 11th, the county government sent personnel to the countryside to inspect and exhume the body in the presence of the murderer. However, due to the hot weather, the stench was unbearable. Although there were many onlookers, they all covered their noses. As a result, it was found that the deceased had a hole in the back of his head from a blow, his left finger was chopped open, and there were strangulation marks on his neck, indicating that he had been strangled to death before being buried. However, it was definitely not the act of one person. The township police then put the coffin in place, and the county government detained Jin Heshang pending investigation.

Letter

Dear Editor, After investigating the news about the Qingdao Minghua Bank that was published in your newspaper on June 6th, it stated that the municipal authorities intended to repay small depositors with savings below 100 yuan in full in advance, and to give the relevant personnel of the bank a reasonable amount of time to repay the remaining deposits. However, the creditors of the Jiaoji Railway objected, and this did not become a reality. After checking, this is not true. The Jiaoji Railway Debt Group has not expressed any objection. We hereby inform your newspaper and hope that you will correct it. Jiaoji Railway Mingyi Debt Group.

Local News

Song Ziwen Invited Banking and Money Industries to a Meeting Yesterday: The Cooperation of the Two Industries Will Stabilize Finance; Centralized Transfer of Funds to the Money Depository Began Yesterday; Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Others Decide to Accept Money Industry's Payment Against Cash

After the Ministry of Finance convened a financial meeting and decided on measures to aid the money industry, the market has become more stable. Song Ziwen, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, convened leaders of the banking and money industries yesterday afternoon, hoping that the banking and money industries would maintain each other and stabilize finance. Centralized transfer of funds to the money depository began yesterday. The Bank Association's subcommittee held a meeting yesterday to decide on the outline and will implement it after contacting the money industry. The Xinxin News Agency reporter has recorded the details as follows:

Meeting of the Two Industries to Cooperate

The difficulties encountered by the Shanghai money industry have been resolved by the financial meeting convened by the Ministry of Finance, and there are no more problems. In order to make the financial situation of the city more stable, Song Ziwen, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Bank of China, held a meeting at the Central Bank's Board Room at 6:30 p.m. yesterday, preparing some refreshments and inviting leaders from the banking and money industries to discuss cooperation between the banking and money industries, supporting each other, and maintaining finance. Present were Chen Xing, Vice President of the Central Bank, Xi Demao, Manager of the Business Bureau, Bei Songsun, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China, Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, Qin Runqing, Chairman of the Money Industry Association, Yu Zuoting of Hengxun, Pei Yunqing of Furun, Liu Wuqiao of Zhiyu, Qian Yuansheng of Jintai, Lin Ruiting of Tongqing, Li Shoushan of Shuntai, Fu Songnian, Chen Shengwu, and more than 20 managers of other money shops. During the meeting, Song Ziwen gave a detailed report on the need for cooperation between the banking and money industries and the maintenance of the money industry. The meeting adjourned at 7:20 p.m.

Money Industry Measures to Be Implemented Separately

The five measures decided by the Money Industry Special Committee, including fund transfers, borrowing against collateral, and discounts, have been approved by the Banking Industry Association, the Comprador Association of Foreign Banks, and the Money Industry Supervision Committee, and have been implemented separately. All fund transfers from banks to money shops must be transferred to the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depository. Money shops will no longer accept fund transfers from banks. The artificial fluctuation of the money market, "Hua Tou Jia Shui," has been suspended from being listed, and is handled by the Money Industry Reserve Depository.

Centralized Fund Transfers Began Yesterday

The case of centralized fund transfers to the Money Industry Reserve Depository, one of the five measures of the Money Industry Association, was approved by an emergency executive committee meeting of the Banking Association. The Banking Association specifically convened an emergency executive committee meeting to discuss and approve it, and stipulated five measures to be followed by all banks. The Xinxin News Agency reporter inquired at the Money Industry Reserve Depository yesterday and learned that centralized fund transfers began partially yesterday and are expected to be fully implemented today. The Banking Association's announcement was just issued yesterday morning, and some banks had already issued fund transfer notes to various money shops the night before. At the same time, the Money Industry Reserve Depository has added staff to handle all matters due to the increased workload after centralized fund transfers.

Subcommittee Meeting Held by Banking and Money Industries Yesterday

The subcommittee organized by the Banking Association held its first meeting at 4:30 p.m. yesterday in the Banking Association's conference room. Present were committee members from nine banks, including the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Xingye Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Dalu Bank, Jin City Bank, Salt Bank, and Zhongnan Bank. Zhu Boquan, manager of the Banking Note Exchange, presided over the meeting, discussing the procedures for centralized fund transfers to the Money Industry Reserve Depository. The meeting adjourned at 6:40 p.m. It is reported that the results of yesterday's meeting have determined the outline and can be implemented immediately after contacting the Money Industry Association. In the future, the procedures for handling fund transfers will be more convenient.

Banking Association Issues Announcement for Compliance

Based on the emergency meeting on the case of unified delivery of fund transfer notes to the Money Depository, the Banking Association issued an announcement yesterday morning to all banks and the Banking Association Joint Reserve Committee for compliance. The original text is as follows: Dear Sirs, After investigating the fact that the Money Industry Association made five new resolutions yesterday to refresh the business of money shops, which have been implemented after public announcement. The first item is, "All fund transfers from banks currently deposited in various money shops must be transferred to the Money Depository at the same time. From now on, money shops will no longer accept fund transfers from banks." This measure is extremely important for the revenue and expenditure of the banking industry. The Association urgently convened an executive committee meeting on the 11th (today) at 2:00 p.m. to discuss the response. The measures decided are as follows: (1) Fund transfers deposited in money shops by all banks until the 11th will be transferred to the Money Depository from the 12th, opening accounts for transactions. (2) In the future, all fund transfer notes from member money shops received by all banks from customers on a daily basis will be sent to the Money Depository. If fund transfer funds are to be used, they will be drawn from the Money Depository. Fund transfer notes received from foreign and non-member money shops will be collected by senior clerks dispatched by the banks. (3) If banks must settle any shortages, they can use fund transfer notes deposited in the Money Depository to settle at market rates. In addition to drawing from the market, the Money Depository can negotiate with the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications for borrowing in case of any shortages. The interest rate will be determined by the three banks. (4) When banks must transport cash to various ports, they can request the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to handle the fund transfer according to the fund transfer procedures. (5) The restrictions on the method of fund transfer funds deposited in the exchange according to the Joint Reserve Committee's Circular No. 74 will continue to apply for the time being. The above resolutions are trial measures, and it has been decided to organize a subcommittee immediately to discuss them in detail. If there are any areas that need improvement, another meeting will be held for discussion and another announcement will be issued. Please comply accordingly. It is also learned that after receiving the above announcement, the Banking Reserve Committee immediately notified all banks of the Note Exchange yesterday morning to comply accordingly.

Supervisory Committee Reviews Collateral

Xu Kan, Du Yuesheng, Qin Runqing, Wang Xiaolai, and Gu Yigu, members of the Money Industry Supervisory Committee, as well as Xu Baoqi (Deputy Manager of the Banking Note Exchange), Hu Meian (Deputy Manager of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank), Shi Jiu'ao (Deputy Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China), Wang Zisong (Manager of the Issuance Department of the Bank of Communications), and others who were additionally appointed by the Ministry of Finance, continued their meeting at the Ningbo Road Money Industry Reserve Depository at 2:00 p.m. yesterday to review the collateral of the money shops in order to issue financial public bonds. The meeting adjourned at approximately 4:00 p.m.

Three Banks Meet to Accept Cash Pledges

The Loan Committee (i.e., the banking group) formed by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications held a meeting at the Central Bank at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. Present were Xi Demao, Manager of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank, Hu Meian, Deputy Manager, Bei Songsun, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China, and Zhang Peishen, Manager of the Business Department of the Bank of Communications, etc. They discussed the money industry's request to pledge financial public bonds to borrow cash. The meeting adjourned at noon. It is reported that the outcome of the consultation was that the money industry's request would be accepted, and the pledge discount would be handled according to the principles decided by the financial meetings held in recent days.

Hurry to Complete Procedures to Join the Exchange

After approval, the Money Industry Joint Reserve Depository is rushing to complete the various procedures for joining the Banking Joint Reserve Committee Note Exchange as an exchanger. According to the New Voice News Agency reporter, according to Article 5 of the Banking Association Note Exchange Regulations, when an exchange bank joins, it should determine one of the following items in the membership fee and pay it to the Association: (1) Silver dollar 1,000 yuan, (2) Silver dollar 500 yuan, (3) Silver dollar 300 yuan. Article 6 stipulates that one of the following items in the security deposit should be determined, and the Association's certificate or cash should be paid to the Association. If cash is paid, rent and interest may be calculated: (1) Silver dollar 30,000 yuan, (2) Silver dollar 20,000 yuan (3) Silver dollar 10,000 yuan. Now the Money Industry Reserve Depository is the central organization of 55 fund transfer money shops, and the matters such as its membership fee, security deposit, and exchange time after joining are all under negotiation. Yesterday, Zhu Boquan, manager of the exchange, and Qin Xiqing, manager of the Money Depository, discussed everything. Due to the complicated procedures, it is expected that they will be able to formally join the exchange tomorrow or the day after. (New Voice News Agency)

The International Savings Society Met Yesterday

After the recent wave of withdrawals at the International Savings Society, it has been quelled thanks to the effective management of the Society. The Chinese and foreign directors of the Society, S. Speelman, F. d'Arnoux, Ye Zhuotang, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Xing, Li Fusun, and Song Ziliang, gathered on the third floor of the Central Bank at 3:00 p.m. yesterday to discuss issues such as the recent wave of withdrawals. The meeting adjourned at 4:30 p.m.

National Products Association Urges Completion of Survey Forms

The Shanghai Citizens' National Products Promotion Association has concrete measures to alleviate the financial difficulties of local industry and commerce. Yesterday, it specifically notified the factories and members under its jurisdiction to urge them to complete the economic survey forms and the amount of loans needed so that they can be compiled and sent to the National Products Alliance for forwarding to the banking group for loan implementation. The notice stated, "Regarding the case of loan relief for industry and commerce in Shanghai, representatives of the Association, including Gu Xiyuan, Lu Xingzhuang, Zhang Zilian, and Chen Yiting, visited Vice Minister Xu to discuss the measures, and Vice Minister Xu approved that the funds designated by the Ministry would be the second guarantee and ordered the banking group to follow the ten principles of loan approval and implement the loan of 15 million yuan against collateral." The notice further stated, "All survey forms previously issued by the Association to various factories, but a few factories have not yet completed and sent them to the Association, please inform the factories and employees of each Association to complete and send them to the Association within three days for forwarding to the banking group for review. It is urgent to inform the Association for implementation." The notice added, "Loan relief is an important condition for the revitalization of the national products industry. Now that the banking group has been established and is raising funds, and the loan approval principles have also been announced, the opportunity is ripe. Members of the industry and commerce are in their current situation, whether they need funds or not, please refer to the previously issued economic survey form and reply to the Association immediately so that it can be forwarded. This is a matter of personal interest, please do not delay."

Japanese Ambassador Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday: Leaving for Beijing Today; Presenting Credentials Tomorrow Morning

According to the Central News Agency, the newly appointed Japanese Ambassador to China, Akira Ariyoshi, arrived in Shanghai by Japanese ship Shanghai Maru at 4:00 p.m. yesterday. He is scheduled to leave for Beijing by express train at 8:00 a.m. this morning to first visit Acting Foreign Minister Wang and will meet with Chairman Lin of the National Government at 11:00 a.m. tomorrow morning to present his credentials. The details of the Japanese Ambassador's arrival in Shanghai and the statements he made are recorded as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

Yesterday afternoon, people from all walks of life in China and Japan went to the Huishan Wharf to welcome Ambassador Ariyoshi to Shanghai, including Yu Ming, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Zhou Li, Secretary, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General representing Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Commissioner Wang Changchun, and from the Japanese side, Matsumoto Tadao, Special Envoy of the Japanese Government visiting China, Horiuchi, Counselor of the Embassy, Yokokawa, Commercial Counselor, Izawa, Military Attaché, Sato, Naval Attaché, Kobeto, Deputy Naval Attaché, Ishii, Consul General in Shanghai, Suma, Consul General in Beijing, Vice Admiral Araki, Commander of the Third Fleet of the Japanese Navy stationed in China, Sugisaka, Commander of the Japanese Navy Landing Forces stationed in Shanghai, and more than 300 Japanese residents.

Arrival Situation

Ambassador Ariyoshi, accompanied by Ariyoshi, Counselor of the Embassy, and Yokokawa, Secretary, departed from Kobe on the Japanese ship Shanghai Maru on the 10th to take office in China. Mrs. Ariyoshi plans to come to China after spending the summer in Japan. The ship was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 3:00 p.m. yesterday, but due to encountering wind en route, it was delayed until approximately 4:00 p.m. before docking at the Huishan Wharf. All welcomers boarded the ship to welcome him after the ship docked, and then disembarked and went to the Japanese Consulate General to rest. At the time of the Ambassador's arrival in Shanghai, the Huishan Wharf was heavily guarded, preventing pedestrians from entering and exiting.

Right: Japanese Ambassador (Left) Yu Ming, Zhu Lai Lin (Photographers)

Spokesman

After the Japanese Ambassador returned to the Consulate General, he met with Chinese news reporters and made the following statement, "I have returned to the country this time to report on the situation of my mission to China. With the elevation of the rank of envoys between the two countries, I have been entrusted with the mission to China, and I should continue the spirit of the past to promote the friendship between the two countries in the future. The Japanese government and the public have great expectations for Sino-Japanese friendship, so after the elevation of the rank of envoys between the two countries, I wish that the relations between the two countries will become even more friendly. As for the issue of Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, it is indeed the only essential factor for promoting the friendship between the two countries. During my return to the country, I have consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the business community several times, but no results have been obtained. As for the issue of moving the embassy to Beijing, the Japanese side has this hope, but it is difficult to find a suitable location in Nanjing for a while, so it is difficult to realize it in the short term. I am scheduled to take the early train to Beijing on the morning of the 13th and meet with Chairman Lin of the National Government at 11:00 a.m. on the morning of the 14th to present my credentials. After staying in Beijing for a short time, I will return to Shanghai.
