Tax Bureau Telegraphically Summons Heads of Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureaus to Shanghai for Meeting: Attendees Include Ten Provinces Such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui; Consultations on the Problem of Consolidating Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Revenue; Meeting to be Held for Two Days Starting on the 20th of This Month

According to the Huadong News Agency, the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance recently telegraphed the heads of the stamp duty, tobacco, and alcohol tax bureaus in ten provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Henan, Fujian, Shandong, Hebei, and Hunan, ordering them to come to Shanghai before the 20th of this month to discuss the issue of consolidating stamp duty, tobacco, and alcohol tax revenue. A reporter specifically visited Mr. Chen, the chief of the General Affairs Section of the department, yesterday morning, who provided the following details:

Scheduled Meeting Wu Qiding, Director of the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance, considers the stamp duty, tobacco, and alcohol tax to be one of the important sources of national revenue. Since taking office, he has repeatedly consolidated it, but so far it has not improved. Moreover, as of the end of March this year, only one or two of the ten or so provinces have been able to collect enough in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Finance, and some have even reported only 30% to 40% of the amount collected. Therefore, in order to make every effort to make up for the shortfall, he specially requested and obtained approval from the Ministry of Finance to convene the heads of the stamp duty, tobacco, and alcohol tax bureaus of various provinces to come to Shanghai for a meeting to discuss concrete measures for consolidation. The meeting date is from 9:00 AM on the 20th of this month, and the meeting will last for two days, closing on the afternoon of the 21st. The meeting location is the conference hall of the department in the Jianghai Customs Building on Hankou Road.

Attending Directors The directors and deputy directors of the stamp duty, tobacco, and alcohol tax bureaus of the provinces designated to attend the meeting include: Jiangsu (Director) Sheng Shengyi, (Deputy) Xue Futian; Zhejiang (Director) Zhao Xi'en, (Deputy) Huang Zupei; Anhui (Director) Jing Lingxin; Hubei (Director) Li Rongkai, (Deputy) Yang Duo; Hunan (Director) Tang Yan, (Deputy) Yi Ding; Jiangxi (Director) Jing Youyan, (Deputy) Pan Linyan; Henan (Director) Qu Dacheng, (Deputy) Lu Tinggan; Fujian (Director) Wang Guanghui; Shandong (Director) Li Zongbi, (Deputy) Chuan Zhengshun; Hebei (Director) Liao Chungao, (Deputy) Xu Xian.

Scope of Discussion According to Mr. Chen, Chief of the General Affairs Section of the Taxation Department, the department has seen a sharp decline in tobacco and alcohol tax revenue in recent years, and at a time when the national treasury is stretched and urgently needs funds, it is necessary to change course and make every effort to make up for the shortfall. This is why the meeting was convened. As for the scope of discussion, there is no specific agenda. The purpose of this meeting is to discuss how to consolidate in order to increase revenue. Therefore, after the directors of various regions arrive at the department, consultations will begin on the 20th. At that time, the provisional opinions of the directors will be adopted, and a concrete method will be jointly formulated, and then each will proceed according to the agreed method, and make every effort to consolidate.

Rural Reconstruction Committee's Peng Xuepei Announces Self-Sufficiency Economic Policy: To Save the Current Crisis in the National Economy, We Can Only Strive to Catch Up on This Path

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, Peng Xuepei, Director of the Secretariat of the Rural Reconstruction Committee, recently announced China's self-sufficiency economic policy on the Central Party Headquarters radio station. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency excerpted the main points as follows:

China was originally a country that could be self-sufficient, but because industry is underdeveloped, most manufactured goods are imported from foreign countries, and because of various reasons, a considerable portion of agricultural products are also imported from foreign countries, which has led to the current crisis in the national economy. To save this crisis, we can only strive to catch up on the path of self-sufficiency. If we adopt a self-sufficiency economic policy, there are several key points that must be noted: (1) We must set a step-by-step plan. It is impossible to achieve self-sufficiency in industrial products and agricultural products all at once. The development of industry cannot be achieved overnight. Only agriculture was originally developed in our country. Although we cannot apply science now, the sophistication of our country's farming methods and the richness of farmers' experience are still highly praised by Europeans and Americans today. If we start with agricultural products first, it is very easy to achieve self-sufficiency in agricultural products. But as long as agricultural products are self-sufficient, there will be no more excess of imports. (2) We must implement planned economy. In a world situation that is so unstable and an economic crisis that is so serious, laissez-faire economic policies are too late. If we want to see results quickly, we must use the power of the government to plan and control at the same time. The first step is to do a considerable amount of investigation and research. The second step is to use the power of the government to improve production. The third step is to use the power of the government to facilitate transportation and sales. These are all responsibilities that should be assumed by the government and done conscientiously, not left to nature. (3) Four parts industry and six parts agriculture. Some people say that China is a country based on agriculture. I don't understand what this sentence means. What is called a "country based on agriculture"? The meaning is extremely vague. It can also be interpreted as a factual issue, simply saying that 80% of China's current population relies on agriculture for food. This is a fact. It can also be interpreted as an ideal issue, saying that Chinese people should value agriculture and should take agriculture as an ideal occupation. This is very debatable. It can also be interpreted as a philosophical issue, talking about the national spirit and the rule of the former kings, and connecting China's ancient political system, philosophical thought, and entire culture to the word "agriculture." That is extremely mysterious. Therefore, it raises the question of whether we should base the country on industry. It is also difficult to define what is called a "country based on industry." It is undoubtedly necessary for China to develop industry, but with such a vast land and such a large population that has been engaged in agriculture for generations, agriculture will always occupy a very important position in China's national economy for a very long period of time. Therefore, valuing industry and not valuing agriculture is also impossible in fact. In Europe, some countries emphasize both agriculture and industry, such as France and Poland. It is said that, generally speaking, it is roughly four parts industry and six parts agriculture. Although this is also an extremely vague statement, from the perspective of a self-sufficiency economic policy, this is indeed the ideal economic state of China in the future. In other words, we hope that in the future, China's industrial products will be largely self-sufficient, and agricultural products will also be largely self-sufficient, and China is indeed qualified to hope to realize this in terms of natural conditions. (4) Industry and commerce should be dispersed throughout the country. The over-concentration of population in cities is a problem that all advanced countries are very concerned about. The disadvantage of cities is that everyone lives a dirty, cramped, and unsanitary life, and everyone is infected with the bad habits that are inevitably attached to cities. The advantage of rural areas is that they are not only beneficial to physical health but also cultivate the virtues of simplicity, honesty, and equality. The result of population concentration in cities is that the country loses the supply of most of its healthy population. Secondly, industry and commerce are concentrated in a very small number of cities. For example, the center of gravity of industry and commerce in our country is almost entirely in Shanghai. This is an extremely dangerous thing in terms of national defense. European countries have already discovered these disadvantages, but the die is cast and it is not easy to transform. When our country begins construction, we should have a new impression in mind and should open a new path. We should make full use of the land and human resources of various places, and make cities and agriculture complement each other and assist each other.

Literacy Education Committee Formulates "Guidelines for Sub-Group Work"

The Shanghai Literacy Education Committee has organized literacy education service groups to make up for the shortcomings of literacy schools. The details have been seen in previous reports. It is now heard that the committee has formulated guidelines for sub-group work for the purpose of clarifying the work of the sub-groups and facilitating their operation. The full text is appended below: (1) After receiving the letter of appointment from the general group (which has already been sent out earlier this week), the head of the sub-group should immediately fill out the form and send it to the general group within three days (the general group is located in the Shanghai Literacy Education Committee in the central district of the city, Zhengzhong Road). (2) After being appointed, the head of the sub-group should immediately recruit members in accordance with Article 5 of the service group charter. Any middle school students or primary school students in grades four, five, and six, or primary school students in grade two who are at least ten years old, can be recruited as members, and please pay attention to the one-fourth quota in Article 16 of the service group charter. (3) When recruiting members, the sub-group head should first or simultaneously look for several deputy heads and report them to the general group for appointment. (4) The recruitment of members for the sub-group should be completed before June 17th. (5) When the recruitment of members is completed, the members should be announced to join the group and a member swearing-in ceremony should be held. The oath is as follows: "I solemnly swear that I will obey the orders of the general group and the sub-group with utmost sincerity, teach people to read, and never be lazy or deceive others. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept punishment. (Name of sub-group in a certain school of the Shanghai Literacy Education Service Group, Signed: [Name], [Date])" (6) After the sub-group is established, a summary table should be filled out and sent to the general group and the Literacy Education Committee, the district office, and the district official. A list of addresses is attached and should be checked. (7) The work of members teaching people should officially begin on July 1st. Each member should teach at least [number of people], and the [number of characters] literacy textbook should be read within [number of months], or within [number of months] at the latest. (Although there is a summer vacation in July, the head of each sub-group and [member] should stay at school at least [number of days] per week to guide members' teaching and call together members, [or] train the public, or conduct testing. Summer vacation is a great opportunity for students to teach people and should not be missed. The sub-group leaders and deputy leaders must stay at school regularly to provide guidance, which is essential.) (8) The volunteer form in Article 10 of the service group charter has already been distributed to each sub-group. If it is not enough, each sub-group should print its own copies. (10) The table in Article 10 of the service group charter, namely the member's teaching diary form, has already been distributed to each sub-group. If it is not enough, it should also be printed by itself. (10) There are two types of literacy textbooks, one for adults and one for children, which are issued by the head of the sub-group to the district office of the Literacy Education Committee. (11) In Article 18 of the previously issued service group charter, the word "term" in the phrase "members in the term" is a mistake for "week". (12) The report procedure in Article 1 of the previously issued "Extra-Curricular Tutoring Measures" may be exempted due to the addition of Item [number] to Article [number] of the service group charter. However, if the district office believes that it is necessary for the volunteer to enter a literacy school after receiving the volunteer form forwarded by the sub-group, it may still order him or her to study at the school.

Five Exchanges Appeal for Delay in Imposing Transaction Tax: Five Exchanges Appoint Du Yuesheng to Petition Kong in Person; Gold Industry Petition Delegation Requests Reduction in Tax Rate

According to the Shiye News Agency, since the five exchanges in the city received the order from the Ministry of Finance to start collecting transaction tax on July 1st, they have all felt that business is sluggish and cannot bear the heavy burden. The group is in a state of panic. The directors of the five exchanges held a joint meeting the day before yesterday to discuss countermeasures. Yesterday, the Gold Industry Brokers Association also held a meeting and submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to approve a reduction in the tax rate in order to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants. The details are as follows:

Meeting of the Directors of the Five Exchanges

The Federation of Five Exchanges convened a joint meeting of the directors of the five exchanges at the board room of the Cotton Exchange at around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. Du Yuesheng of the Gold Exchange, Mu Ouchu of the Cotton Exchange, Zhang Weiru of the Securities Exchange, Wang Yiting of the Flour Exchange, Gu Xinrong of the Grain Exchange, and Chu Qiaqing and other six people attended. After a close discussion for [number of hours] hours, the meeting adjourned. A reporter visited Mr. Mu Ouchu yesterday, who said that the content of the meeting was specifically to discuss ways to request the Ministry of Finance to take into account the difficulties of the merchants and approve a delay in the collection of the new tax, and there was no other discussion. Subsequently, according to inquiries made by the reporter to relevant parties, the directors of the five exchanges have resolved to submit a request to the Ministry of Finance, and have appointed Du Yuesheng, the director of the Gold Exchange, as the plenipotentiary representative to personally visit Minister Kong with the petition within the next few days to plead for the matter.

Gold Industry Decides to Form a Petition Delegation

The Gold Exchange Brokers Association convened a general meeting of members at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than 100 members, including Zhan Liansheng, Wang Jiafu, and Wang Yingchang, attended. After Chairman Zhan Liansheng reported the purpose of the meeting, the discussion began on how to request a reduction in the transaction tax scheduled to be collected by the Ministry of Finance. It was resolved to submit a request for a reduction as soon as possible in order to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants. Chairman Zhan immediately read out the draft submitted to the Ministry of Finance and expressed that, in addition to submitting a request for a reduction, the entire petition delegation would be organized according to the resolution of the previous general meeting to petition Minister Kong. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Request for Approval of Reduction Submitted to the Ministry of Finance Yesterday

Zhan Liansheng, President of the Gold Industry Brokers Association, and Wang Jiafu, Vice President, submitted a document to Minister Kong yesterday, stating: "A document is hereby submitted requesting that the implementation of the transaction tax be delayed, as the circumstances of the association are special and adherence to the regulations would hinder business. We earnestly lay out our difficulties in the hope that you will grant us a reduction to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants. The association has repeatedly submitted requests for a reduction on various grounds, and we believe that they have been thoroughly examined by your esteemed leadership, but we have not yet received a reply and are deeply apprehensive. Now we have received an order to start collecting the tax on July 1st, and we are shocked and horrified. We have found that the transactions of our association are different from those of other commodities. Gold transactions are related to international exchange rates, because most countries implement the gold standard. In order to avoid losses in settlement prices, merchants in our country who trade with foreign countries must first hedge in the exchange market. However, the exchange market changes rapidly, and the buying and selling of gold also changes frequently with changes in gold prices. The commission charged by our association is particularly low, which is also for a reason, so that the cost of hedging is reduced and facilitated. Now, the tax rate set by your ministry is, in terms of reasonable assessment, not too large, but other commodities have procedures for import and export, and there is no situation of import and export at the same time. Only gold hedging changes with market prices, and there are even cases of import and export several times in one transaction. Each time, the tax must be paid, which in effect is heavier than that of other commodities. Therefore, the gold transaction tax is already a heavy burden compared to the commission collected by the association. If the current tax rate is implemented, the business will inevitably decrease sharply, and the state tax revenue will not increase. This is the special circumstance of the association, and adherence to the regulations would hinder business. The association is not making specious arguments or hoping for unreasonable gains, but is sincerely considering the state treasury and the situation of the merchants, and must take both into consideration. In this time of commercial warfare and economic decline, foreign trade is always in a state of turmoil. The government has spared no effort in protecting and rescuing merchants, and all the people are deeply grateful. For this hedging mechanism that is related to international trade, there will surely be compassion and fulfillment. Therefore, we dare to lay out our innermost feelings and make a final request, hoping that you will grant us a reduction, which would be a great blessing for the overall situation and for the association."

Ministry of Justice Approves the Provision of Security with Bonds

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously requested the Ministry of Justice to approve the issuance of a circular to all courts not to refuse to accept the provision of security with public treasury bonds by litigants, based on the request of the Shanghai Timber Industry Association. After the association submitted its request on the 28th of last month, it received a reply from the Ministry of Justice yesterday with approval number 1673, stating: "The content of the report is understood. The matters mentioned are indeed factual. With regard to applications for provisional seizure, when the court orders the provision of appropriate security, cash should be deposited or valuable securities deemed appropriate by the court should be substituted. According to the provisions of Paragraph 1 of Article 102 of the current Civil Procedure Law, the court has the right to exercise discretion. However, if the creditor provides reliable and valuable securities that have been converted into a corresponding amount at the current market price as security within the scope permitted by laws and regulations, the court may facilitate it. Furthermore, such cases of provisional seizure are often urgent and should be handled expeditiously to prevent the debtor from concealing assets. This matter has been ordered by the ministry to the Jiangsu High Court, the Second and Third Branches of the Jiangsu High Court, and the courts under their jurisdiction to comply with."

Ningbo Fellow Association Sends Personnel to Investigate Relief Efforts

The Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association previously requested permission to exempt taxes on 50,000 piculs of foreign rice passports in the Ningbo area, which suffered from a severe drought, in order to prepare relief rice and stabilize prices for relief. However, due to the time required for procurement and the urgent need of the victims, it was resolved to first advocate the use of Ningbo rice merchants and entrust Zhuo Baoting of the Ningbo Taihe Rice Company to handle the matter nearby, and to establish a preparation office for relief rice at the Fifth District Administrative Inspectorate of Zhejiang Province to coordinate the overall work. Later, it was discovered that the broken Siamese rice received by the recipients of the subsidized rice in Yin and Feng counties was of poor quality, being stale, rotten, and moldy. Accusations arose, and the Tenth All-County Representative Assembly of Yin County believed that the rice merchants deliberately mixed in inferior rice and resolved to severely punish the person in charge, Zhuo Baoting, and requested the Yin County government to detain Zhuo Baoting. The Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association, upon hearing the news, believed that Mr. Zhuo was usually very enthusiastic about local public welfare and would not engage in private gain in this relief effort. It was suspected that he was taking the blame for others. It immediately telegraphed the Yin County government to restore Zhuo's freedom and dispatched Yan Boying, a member of the association, to Ningbo to investigate the matter and clarify the truth. It is now heard that 32 Ningbo rice merchants, including Fengtai, believe that the occurrence of the case is related to their business reputation and jointly sent a letter to the association yesterday to explain. The letter reads: "We respectfully report that Zhuo Baoting, the manager of our fellow merchant Taihe Rice Company, was entrusted by your association to handle the subsidized rice, but was accused by the Yin County Party Department of mixing in inferior rice and taking the opportunity to collect money because of the discovery of moisture, clumping, worms, and mold, and was ordered by the Yin County government to detain and punish him, and was not allowed to post bail. We are extremely grateful that your association sent letters and telegrams and was able to temporarily allow bail. However, the case has not been clarified, and not only is Mr. Zhuo's personal reputation at stake, but also the business credit of our fellow merchants has been swept away. The original plan was for 50,000 piculs of subsidized rice to be prepared at one time, but Mr. Zhuo believed that market prices were unpredictable, so only 16,500 piculs have been prepared so far. Considering the recent prices, if the full amount had been prepared, we do not know how much would have been lost. This can be used as proof of loyalty and diligence. As for the quality of the rice, there are often differences in the rice purchased from the same location at the same price. If we talk about moisture, clumping, worms, and mold, it may be due to moisture in the warehouse or due to weather conditions, which is an unavoidable fact. It is said that rice merchants work hard and get tired in April. Unexpectedly, we have been blamed by all parties. The party and government authorities have severely punished us. Mr. Zhuo's innocence is not important, but the lack of clarity is related to the reputation and credit of our fellow merchants. Therefore, we dare to take the liberty of submitting this report jointly, hoping that your association will send a special commissioner to Ningbo as soon as possible to investigate the matter together. The matter is important, and we hope that you will implement it quickly."

City Chamber of Commerce Notifies Various Businesses Regarding New Regulations for Import Duty Payment Certificates

A person from the public sphere says, the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to various trade associations in the city stating: "Regarding the matter that on the 7th of this month, we received letter No. 1450 from the Jianghai Customs, which stated: 'After examining the import duty payment, the forms have now been revised and will be implemented from the 10th of this month. This new type of import duty payment certificate will be filled out by the Customs according to the format and issued free of charge. Merchants do not need to fill it out themselves. The new import duty payment certificate should be submitted together with the import declaration form. After the Customs verifies and fills in the various tax items, four copies will be given to the merchants, who should take them to the Central Bank Tax Collection Office to pay the taxes according to the regulations. After paying the taxes, the merchants should return the first and second copies to the Customs as proof that the taxes have been paid. The import tax receipt will henceforth be issued by the Customs to the taxpayer for safekeeping. For goods subject to consolidated tax, after the above regulations are implemented, merchants must still fill out the consolidated tax payment certificate when preparing the import declaration form and submit it for verification. All merchants should be informed accordingly. This notice is hereby issued.' We are sending this letter to notify you to take note and act accordingly."

Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Court, Explaining That Delivery Notes Do Not Require Stamps

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, to explain the reason why delivery notes do not require stamps, wrote to the Jiangsu Shanghai Local Court, stating: "Regarding the matter that on the 11th of this month, we received a letter from the Local Timber Trade Association stating that the Ruichang Timber Firm, a member of their association, had recently been investigated by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, who seized seven delivery notes last month. On the 7th of this month, they received Criminal Ruling No. 272, Series 24, from the Shanghai Local Court, sentencing them to a fine of 70 yuan. They requested assistance, etc. Having investigated the delivery notes, they only contain the dimensions and quantity of the goods and do not indicate any amount of money. They are issued for customers to check the quantity of goods. At the same time, there is also an invoice, and when receiving payment, there is also a tear-off slip and receipt, all of which have the required stamps affixed. There is no case of missing stamps. The court considers the delivery note as an invoice, which is due to a lack of understanding of the customs of the trade. In addition to Ruichang Firm filing a separate appeal against the ruling, we are sending this letter to convey the situation. We respectfully request that you consider the difficulties of the business community and carefully review the matter, sending a letter to the Local Court to make corrections according to the law. We would be extremely grateful." Two sample notes, each on a separate sheet, were enclosed with the letter. After examining the two sample notes, not only are the colors different, but the content recorded is also different. The latter type, which is called a delivery note, focuses on recording the dimensions and number of pieces and is like a quantity list attached to the invoice. This delivery note is sent along with the invoice when the goods are shipped. Therefore, there are definitely no two duplicate invoices for one shipment. This is also a common practice in the business world. Furthermore, on February 18th of the 15th year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Finance issued Directive No. 9822 to the Shaoxing Oil Trade Association, which stated that if the item slip is sent along with a stamped invoice, then the item slip can be exempt from stamps. This shows that for the convenience of merchants, a separate item slip is issued in addition to the invoice to assist with the process. Regardless of the name used, as long as the invoice has sufficient stamps affixed and is sent with the goods, the latter type of item slip no longer needs to have stamps affixed. This has been a long-standing precedent. We are sending this letter with the relevant information for your court's reference."

Scarce Rainfall Causes Rice Prices to Rise Daily

Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been very dry, with very little rainfall. Recently, rice prices have also been rising, causing considerable anxiety among the people. We have investigated the situation as follows:

Farmers Hope for Rain Since the drought in the rice-producing areas last year caused a severe crop failure, people have been in a state of anxiety. This year, since the beginning of summer, the rice seedlings in the fields have been in dire need of rain, but the sky has not rained. In the Jiangsu and Zhejiang areas, if there is no heavy rain, the early rice crop will be affected. Although there have been showers in the city in recent days, the area covered is very small. Therefore, the farmers in the various villages are all in a state of panic.

Rice Prices Rise According to the rice market in the city, even though there is a severe credit crunch, rice prices are still rising daily. Although they had fallen slightly a few days ago, they have recently exceeded 13.5 yuan. This is because the supply from the interior is scarce, and those who hoard rice are unwilling to sell it, resulting in a shortage of rice in the market and a daily increase in prices. If rainfall cannot be evenly distributed this year, the future of the people's food supply is worrying.

Taicang Native Association Telegraphed the Provincial Government to Strictly Prohibit the Releasing of Lake Fields to Alleviate Lake Calamities and Relieve the People's Hardships

The Taicang Native Association in Shanghai yesterday telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Construction Department, stating: "Chen, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and Shen, Director of the Construction Department, the water conservancy of the Three Wu regions is centered on Taihu Lake. In recent years, downstream counties have suffered frequent droughts and floods, which are attributed to the mismanagement of Taihu Lake. Furthermore, tenants along the river are competing to enclose the lake for farming, gradually reducing the lake's area. The lake water cannot be contained, and the ability to store floodwater is lost. Droughts will occur imminently. As a result, downstream counties, such as our Taicang, are directly affected. The ignorance of the common people in seeking profit is understandable. However, the Lake Field Clearance Office and the local county government not only fail to stop them but openly organize large-scale companies to pay for the right to reclaim land. They were deceived at the time and are now trying to cover up the matter. We do not know what their intentions are. The Lou River is an important channel for draining water from Taihu Lake and is also the center of water conservancy for all farmland in Taicang County. If the lake surface is occupied, the water source will gradually be blocked. Once droughts and floods occur, the 800,000 mu of farmland will be rendered unusable. This matter concerns the interests of the entire county. We have no choice but to jointly telegraph your office (department) to thoroughly investigate the facts, remove all enclosed lake fields and restore them to the lake, and strictly prohibit the release of lake fields in order to alleviate lake calamities and relieve the people's hardships. We await your urgent orders." Respectfully submitted by Hu Duanxing, Yang Zhihao, Lu Jingshi, Shen Boli, Jin Xiawen, Zhao Boying, He Yuanming, Zhu Jingan, Hong Jingping, Qian Weizong, Wu Yulin, Wu Shenyi, Qian Gongdu, Gong Minqiu, Shao Menggang, and others from the Shanghai Taicang Native Association.

Zhu Xiangcheng was Suddenly Assassinated After Arriving in Shanghai from Ningbo in the Early Morning. He Knew Someone Was Plotting Against Him and Went to Ningbo and Shanghai to Temporarily Avoid Danger. He Was Shot and Killed by Two Thugs After Landing Yesterday Morning.

Zhu Xiangsheng, a 21-year-old from Yuyao, Zhejiang, resided at No. 19, Baoqing Lane, No. 666, Tiantong Road. His father, Nuo Zengxuan, owned the Huichang Exchange Shop in Xingren Lane, Ningbo Road, with very rich assets. Xiangsheng was the only son. After his father passed away seven years ago, Xiangsheng was too young to continue his father's business. Therefore, his mother decided to close the shop. The estate was about 200,000 yuan. The year after his father's death, Xiangsheng was kidnapped and a huge ransom was demanded. His mother asked someone to negotiate with the kidnappers and reluctantly paid 30,000 yuan to redeem him. At the age of 18 and a half, his mother arranged for him to marry the daughter of Xie Shaogeng, a wealthy businessman from the same hometown. After the marriage, the couple had disagreements and divorced within a year, paying 8,000 to 9,000 yuan in alimony, spending a total of 70,000 yuan. His mother passed away in Shanghai after the January 28th Incident. All the estate was inherited by Xiangsheng alone. Recently, he became addicted to opium and did not work, living off his assets, which have been depleted by more than half. He has not remarried. He rents out part of his house in Shanghai to his cousin Chen Shuitang (over 30 years old, manager of the Hongchang Rice Shop at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Park Road). Last autumn, his family suffered misfortune again when they were robbed by bandits who stole several thousand yuan. Around the end of last year, Xiangsheng suddenly received bad news that someone wanted to plot against him. Therefore, from the first month of the lunar calendar this year until recently, he frequently traveled between Shanghai and Ningbo, with no fixed schedule, hoping to avoid danger. He always traveled on the Taikoo Steamship Company's Shanghai-Ningbo route on the new Beijing steamship. This time, he went to Ningbo on Monday of this week and took the new Beijing steamship from Ningbo to Shanghai on the 10th, staying in a first-class cabin, room number 12. After the ship arrived at the port at 5:30 a.m. on the 10th, Xiangsheng landed at about 6:00 a.m. and walked north along the Bund to hire a car to return home. Unexpectedly, when he walked to the sidewalk near the Company Wharf and the Shanghai Observatory on Yangjingbang, next to a cigarette booth, two thugs suddenly rushed up from behind, one wearing a gray long gown and the other wearing a blue long gown. The thug wearing the blue long gown took out a pistol and fired at Xiangsheng's back. With a loud bang, the bullet entered Xiangsheng's back and went straight through his chest near the left breast without exiting. Xiangsheng fell to the ground, and blood gushed out like a fountain, and he died instantly. At that time, there were few pedestrians on the road. The murderers, seeing that their goal had been achieved, quickly fled without a trace. The French Concession Maitland Police Station received the news and immediately sent a large number of detectives to apprehend them. However, it was too late, and the murderers had already fled far away. Therefore, they carried the body to the forensic examination office of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch and sent detectives to investigate the relatives of the deceased. At that time, the deceased's cousin Chen Shuitang, cousin Nuo Housheng (28 years old, living at No. 2, Lane 433, North Shansi Road, running a gold exchange business), and cousin Zhu Hongsheng (running an exchange business) had already arrived at the forensic examination office after hearing the news. Subsequently, the police station reported to the Special Second District Court Prosecutor's Office, which dispatched Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with Forensic Doctor Wei, Clerk Zhao, etc., to inspect the body at noon and remove the bullet. After the examination, they sat down at the desk. According to Detective Zhang Chunsheng's report on the investigation after the incident, the officials questioned the deceased's relatives, Zhu Housheng, Zhu Hongsheng, and Chen Shuitang, about the deceased's life. They ruled that Zhu Xiangsheng died from gunshot wounds sustained while alive. The body was handed over to the relatives Zhu Housheng and Zhu Hongsheng for burial. The bullet and a note were ordered to be investigated and then submitted to the case file. After the examination, according to the relatives, the deceased did not usually go out often. It is difficult to determine the reason for his sudden death. The French police planned to search the deceased's residence in the hope of obtaining clues to the murderers. They have also dispatched detectives to purchase leads and arrest the murderers. The remains of the deceased were approved by the family to be transported to the China Funeral Home for encoffining.

The First Branch of the First District Municipal Union Urges a Rent Reduction Declaration

The Shanghai Special District Citizen's First District Branch Nanjing Road Commercial Union issued a declaration urging rent reduction for its member stores, stating: "In recent years, the commercial market has been in a state of depression and has reached its extreme. The sound of bankruptcies and liquidations is heard from time to time. Nanjing Road in Shanghai, which has always been known as prosperous, has seen its stores' business decline daily. The future is deeply feared. Without seeking salvation, how can we survive? The causes of today's market decline are not just one. While the method of salvation is best focused on addressing the root cause, this cannot be achieved overnight. It requires the unified planning of the upper and lower levels of society to be effective. Now, the urgent task is to treat the symptoms, which is nothing more than increasing revenue and reducing expenses. However, the increase in revenue for businesses, that is, the increase in customers' purchasing power, has already become an irreversible fact. Therefore, we have to retreat and seek a plan to reduce expenses. According to general merchants, the largest monthly expenditure is rent, especially for stores on Nanjing Road, which account for more than 60% of the total expenses. In the past, during prosperous times, it was still possible to barely support it. In these times of decline in all industries, it is really unbearable. Some even find that their annual hard work is not enough to pay their rent. There are even those who are sued for rent arrears or go bankrupt as a result. Now, in order to save businesses and adjust the market, the first priority is to reduce rent to slightly ease the difficulties of businesses. The prosperity of the market is directly proportional to the increase in land and housing prices, and the decline of the market is directly proportional to the reduction in land and housing prices. The ownership of land and housing belongs to the owners, but it is the stores rented by tenants that cause the price to increase. Now, the tenants cannot bear the high prices of the past. Consider reducing and exempting rent to slightly alleviate the difficulties of the tenants and gradually restore the market. This is actually to alleviate the difficulties faced by the landlords themselves. After all, the financial resources of landlords are stronger than those of tenants who rent houses, and they can turn around more easily. Reducing and exempting a certain percentage of rent is not as difficult for them to cope with as it is for tenants. To put it bluntly, if you are greedy in the present and unwilling to sacrifice, it will make the merchants unable to support themselves and eventually lead to closure. The prosperous streets will surely become a tragic scene with ten houses empty. The landlords' losses will be several times greater than today and will eventually lead to mutual destruction. Therefore, some enlightened landlords have already voluntarily reduced rent or allowed the tenants' requests and implemented it. However, we have rarely heard of it on Nanjing Road. Moreover, the rent standards are very uneven. The same building has different rental prices depending on the person. The amount for the same house differs by several times. Therefore, we should appeal to the landlords on Nanjing Road to quickly broaden their horizons, implement rent reductions, and strive to overcome this unprecedented difficult situation together and achieve a state of coexistence and co-prosperity. Then, recovery is hopeful, and social prosperity is mutually beneficial, not only for the tenants. We hereby declare this, hoping that you will all take note of it."

Preparatory Office for the Establishment of the Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall Holds Founders' Meeting

If you have any proposals, please submit them in writing to this office by the 18th of this month for inclusion in the special publication and for discussion. We hope that you will attend enthusiastically at the time to jointly plan the progress. In addition to sending separate invitations and newspaper advertisements, this notice is specially issued. Furthermore, since this office has accepted Mayor Wu's opinion and decided to convert the bronze statue into a memorial hall, and has received affirmative replies from a majority of the founders, the name of this office should be changed to reflect the facts, and the words "Bronze Statue" should be deleted and its name corrected as follows: "Provisional Preparatory Office for the Establishment of the Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall by Various Circles in Shanghai" This is stated in conjunction.

Newly Appointed President of the District Court, Luo Tong, Held Inauguration Ceremony Yesterday

Luo Tong, the newly appointed president of the Shanghai District Court, was scheduled to be sworn in on the 12th of this month, as previously reported. Yesterday marked the date. At 9:00 AM, guests arrived one after another. Subsequently, the Jiangsu High Court appointed Shen Yuanshan, the presiding judge of the Civil Division of the High Court, to come to Shanghai by car to supervise the oath-taking ceremony. President Luo, along with Pang Shurong, the presiding judge of the Civil Division, and Secretary Wang Xun, greeted them separately. Representatives from various agencies attended, including Zheng Yue, the chief prosecutor of the High Court Branch, Liang Renjie, the president of the High Court Third Branch, Zhao Shibei, the chief prosecutor of the High Court Third Branch, Guo Yun Guan, the president of the First Special District Court, Xiang Youjun, the chief prosecutor of the First Special District Court, Si Mo, the president of the Second Special District Court, Chen San, the chief prosecutor of the Second Special District Court, Hu Renqing, the warden of the Third Prison, and Sun Kui Fang, the director of the Forensic Research Institute. Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of Shanghai, Pan Zhongjia, the magistrate of Shanghai County, Cai Jinjun, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, Xu Yuyin, the chief of the County Public Security Bureau, Deng Peiyi and Chen Shijun from the Security Department, Mao Yun from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Shen Junru from the Lawyers' Association, lawyers Yi Shizhao, Jiang Ping, Zhan Jifeng, Shan Yuhua, and prominent businessmen Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, and over fifty others first went to the reception room upstairs for tea and refreshments. At ten o'clock, a bell rang, and the oath-taking ceremony began. President Luo, accompanied by the guests, went to the First Court. Zhong Shangbin, the chief prosecutor of the District Court, also attended the ceremony. Judicial police chief Zhang Shuping, deputy chief Chen Xihui, and police officers Liu Fu and Gu Hanqing supervised all the bailiffs to maintain order around the hall. The oath supervisor took the chairman's seat, the oath-takers took their positions, and everyone stood in solemn silence. The Party song was sung, the highest respect was paid to the Party and national flag, and three bows were performed. The chairman read the Premier's will, followed by three minutes of silence. The oath supervisor delivered an instruction, followed by speeches from the guests and a response from the oath-taker. After the ceremony, photographs were taken. The oath-taker's oath was as follows: "I, Yu Jing, swear that I will恪遵 (kè zūn - respectfully abide by) the Premier's will, obey the Party's principles, abide by national laws, be loyal and diligent in my duties, and be frugal in expenses. I will never employ useless personnel, engage in corruption or bribery. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept the Party's most severe punishment. This oath." Shen Yuanshan, the commissioner from Jiangsu High Court, stated in his address: "Our country has advocated judicial independence for more than twenty years. The new-style courts that have been established are gradually taking shape and achieving remarkable results. Shanghai, formerly under the jurisdiction of Songjiang, was偏 (piān - secluded) in a corner. Now it is a large port where people from all directions杂处 (záchǔ - mingle). The social situation is inevitably changing rapidly, and the methods of litigation inevitably involve various tricks. The District Court handles civil and criminal cases and bears a great responsibility. Therefore, the Ministry has selected President Luo to lead this court, naturally to choose the right person for the job and to promote improvement. Now that the oath-taking ceremony is being held, I will briefly mention the matters that should be noted. Judicial officials place great importance on integrity. In the past, Yang Zhen's 'Four Knows' were taken as the golden rule by those who were determined to be廉洁 (liánjié - incorruptible). Moreover, in the courtroom, we advocate the rule of law; how can we ignore this? This is one. The dignity of a judge is related to the public's outlook. The slightest carelessness in behavior is enough to bring about criticism. It must be known that judges are entrusted with the lives and property of the people. Even if they abide by the law and perform their duties honestly, they are still afraid of overlooking something. If they are unbridled, they will be guilty. When they reflect on themselves in the quiet of the night, how can they deal with themselves? This is two. The main point of judgment is nothing more than upholding impartiality. Regardless of how evidence is collected or how laws are applied, we must strive for衡 (héng - balance) between human feelings and reason, with impartiality and not allowing the guilty to escape being our goal. This is three. Accumulation of lawsuits, whether civil or criminal, is enough to harm the people. Although sometimes they are restrained by procedures, we should strive to proceed quickly and尽 (jìn - fulfill) our duties. This is four. Judicial organs are most concerned about preventing the asking for favors and the beginning of extortion. In the past, petty officials, clerks, or runners, either because their income was insufficient,罗织 (luózī - fabricated) and陷 (xiàn - framed), or because they were not sufficiently润笔 (rùnbǐ - bribed),蒙蔽 (méngbì - concealed) and delayed. All of these have been criticized by the world. In order to prevent微 (wēi - the slightest hint of evil) before it arises, all the officials, police, and丁役 (dīngyì - servants) of the court must be strictly investigated at all times by officials to prevent them from extorting under the guise of various excuses. Many evils will arise. Not only that, but all judicial administrative affairs are closely related to the handling of cases. If one can work tirelessly and in an orderly manner, the results will be seen more quickly. This is five. The above points have either been seen in brilliant ministerial orders or are the圭臬 (guīniè - standards) that judicial officials should adhere to. As the head of the organization,督 (dū - supervise) colleagues and pay attention to it at all times, so that they do not become lazy over time. President Luo is talented and determined not to be afraid of difficulties, not to be苟 (gǒu - perfunctory), and to整頓 (zhěngdùn - rectify) with the aim of people's happiness," and so on. Next, Mao Yun, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a speech. Shen Junru then stated that the position of the judiciary is important, and it is necessary to distinguish between public and private matters and work hard. Wang Xiaolai then spoke, saying that the movement to publicize unjust imprisonments has recently been launched, and he hopes that all judges will work hard and conscientiously. Finally, after Zhang Shizhao finished his speech, the conclusion was announced.

The Shanghai Municipal Council Decides to Organize a Telephone Committee and Hire Expert Brown

Yesterday (Wednesday) was the date for the regular meeting of the board of directors of the Public Concession工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council). Among the items listed on the agenda, the telephone issue was one of them. The chairman first announced that the French Concession工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) had previously sent a letter to this council regarding the organization of a special telephone committee. The French Concession authorities do not intend to formally send personnel to participate, but they intend to send one observer to attend and listen. This is because the局 (jú - council) intends to hire an expert to engage in a financial study of the telephone issue. The Shanghai Telephone Company has also expressed its agreement with the French工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council)'s proposal. In view of this, the chairman suggested that the special committee be composed of about four to five people, including one each from China, Japan, England, and the United States, or one person elected from residents of other nationalities to participate. This proposal was immediately approved by the entire board of directors, and it was decided that the names of the committee members would be formally submitted at the next regular meeting. The chairman then reported that the工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) had previously telegraphed the British Post Office, asking the authorities to transfer a telephone expert to Shanghai to assist in telephone matters. The British Post Office has now replied in agreement and has recommended Major Brown, the current deputy chief engineer of the British Post Office, as suitable for this position. Mr. Brown has extensive experience in telephone issues and has made many contributions to the construction and maintenance costs of the British telephone industry. He has also personally participated in the revision of British telephone rates, so he is quite suitable for Shanghai's current needs. Mr. Brown will soon retire from the British Post Office and is expected to arrive in Shanghai in early September. After the chairman's report, all directors unanimously decided to reply by telegram to hire Mr. Brown and urge him to travel as soon as possible.

Customs Seizes Smuggled Artificial Silk; Japanese Consulate to Negotiate with Customs

The 大美晚報 (Dà Měi Wǎnbào - Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury) reports that the Chinese Customs巡船 (xúnchuán - patrol boat) "Guanwei" (关卫号) recently seized a Japanese汽油船 (qìyóuchuán - motorboat) at the mouth of the Yangtze River. The ship was carrying artificial silk worth 100,000 yuan. According to regulations, the ship and cargo should be confiscated. However, the captain of the巡船 (xúnchuán - patrol boat), Mr. White格 (gé - ge), has submitted an affidavit to the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai, stating that he wrote in the ship's log that the Japanese汽油船 (qìyóuchuán - motorboat) was detained not in Chinese territorial waters but in international waters five miles east of Amherst Rock. It is expected that the Japanese authorities will demand the return of the ship and cargo from the Chinese Customs based on this affidavit. According to Mr. White格 (gé - ge), who spoke to the Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury today (the tenth), he has resigned from the海关 (hǎiguān - customs) and said he issued the affidavit because海关 (hǎiguān - customs) refused to give him one-tenth of the value of the seized artificial silk as a reward, and instead planned to split it with the captain of a nearby ship that provided his patrol boat with gasoline on that day. He felt that this treatment was unfair, so he was angry and gave the statement. The 大美晚報 (Dà Měi Wǎnbào - Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury) reporter also inquired at the Japanese Consulate, which confirmed that it had Mr. White格 (gé - ge)'s affidavit but did not want to reveal how it would use it. It is also reported that the Japanese Consul has already begun to negotiate with the海关 (hǎiguān - customs) about this matter.

The Shanghai Municipal Council's One-Year Report on Rickshaw Management

The Public Concession工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council)'s rickshaw management office's report for the month of May has been submitted to the board of directors for approval. The report includes a summary of the results since the office was established and a detailed statement on the improvements in rickshaw affairs in the Public Concession. The main points are as follows: The registration of rickshaw owners has been effective. The names and addresses of the big and small句头 (jùtóu - rickshaw gang leaders) have also been recorded. Since the implementation of the revised rickshaw rental regulations approved by the工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) board of directors, the average number of times per month that rickshaw pullers rent (承租) cars is fifteen. In addition to enjoying the various benefits of the mutual aid society, their monthly income has increased by more than several yuan compared to last year.

The total number of registered public rickshaw pullers was 32,015 at the end of May. Private rickshaw pullers have also been registered and are required to wear armbands. Price lists have been affixed to all public rickshaws in prominent locations, with separate payment methods for calculating prices by time and distance.

The rickshaw management office has new-style rickshaws on display, which are greatly improved compared to the old-style rickshaws. The lighting equipment is also good, and the cost is far less than one hundred yuan. The detailed structural drawings can be obtained from the office.

The inspection of ordinary rickshaws is stricter than before, and the police are continuing to crack down on the illegal operation of "野鷄 (yějī - unregulated)"包車 (bāochē - chartered) rickshaws.

The above measures have been informally discussed with the neighboring authorities by the工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) personnel, and the officials are expected to cooperate.

Public Concession Postpones Redemption of Public Bonds This Year

Regarding the redemption of the Shanghai Public Concession工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) six-percent public bonds issued in 1925, the board of directors has decided to postpone the automatic redemption of the bonds for this year. These bonds were issued in 1925 with a total value of 5.6 million taels, and the redemption period was to begin after ten years and end after thirty years. The first self-determined redemption period was December 31 of this year. However, when the director of the Finance Department submitted the tenth-year financial report and the budget proposal for this year at a meeting of the Finance Committee of the工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) on April 2, he proposed that the bonds scheduled to be redeemed this year be postponed. After repeated discussions by the Finance Committee, this matter was reported to the board of directors, which approved the proposal yesterday.

###枇杷 (Pípá - Loquat) Merchants Negotiate with the Fruit Trade Association

Tangxi, Zhejiang, is a large town near the provincial capital of Hangzhou. In addition to rice and silk, farmers rely on 白沙 (Báishā - White Sand)枇杷 (pípá - loquats) as their main source of income. The fresh and sweet quality of these loquats is unparalleled elsewhere. Every harvest season, Tangxi枇杷 (pípá - loquat) merchants mainly transport their goods to the Sixteen Pu fruit market in this city. According to these merchants, the Dragon Boat Festival in the lunar calendar is the peak season for the sale of these枇杷 (pípá - loquats). Therefore, according to custom, each merchant ships their goods to Shanghai to meet the needs of the wholesalers. Normally, the pre-festival sales price would increase, and the profits would be used to offset the price drops after the festival. This year, over sixty merchant ships fully loaded with枇杷 (pípá - loquats) arrived in Shanghai to meet the market demand. However, when the ships arrived at the Sixteen Pu码头 (mǎtou - wharf), they were suddenly affected by the labor dispute between the fruit trade wholesalers and the栈司 (zhànsī - warehouse staff), causing the large quantities of枇杷 (pípá - loquats) to be delayed and sold after the festival, resulting in a loss of approximately ten thousand yuan. The merchants suffered a heavy loss. That evening, the sixty-plus merchant ships held an emergency meeting in a certain place in Nanshi and unanimously resolved that the extreme conflict between the fruit and vegetable industry and the warehouse staff disregarded the sale of the merchants' goods, causing huge losses. However, the warehouse staff were laborers and had no transaction relationship with the merchants, while the wholesalers and merchants had a deep-seated relationship based on years of transactions. Therefore, it was decided that compensation for this loss should be requested from the Fruit Trade Association. Wang Fuqing and Lu Lantian were appointed as representatives to negotiate with the association the other day, but no satisfactory result was achieved. It is now reported that the merchants will petition the Party and government authorities in the near future for assistance.

Concubine of Ma Hongkui Sues to Establish Status; Trial Concludes; Judgment Scheduled for 17th

After the late Ma Fuqi, the father of human rights activist Ma Hongkui, and his widow's eldest daughter-in-law, Ma Chen (the wife of Ma Hongkui), became involved in a will dispute with her brother-in-law, Ma Honggen, and his concubine, Ma Shi, a woman named Qin from Nanjing, along with her son Lushan, claimed to be Ma Hongkui's concubine and hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the Civil Division of the Second Special Court, requesting Ma Chen and her children, Luzhen and Luying, to confirm her status. The trial, which has been opened and witnessed by Judge Tu Shenjie, has been reported in this newspaper many times. The court convened again yesterday at Civil Division 7 under Judge Tu. Both parties were represented by lawyers. The court also summoned Ma Honggen to testify. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that Song Defu recently sent a letter to his lawyer, claiming that he knew the inside story of the Ma family and, after learning of the lawsuit between Qin and Chen, he was willing to testify. Mr. Song was listening in the courtroom and requested the court to call him to testify. The judge approved and ordered Song to be called to the stand. According to Song, he and the Ma family were relatives, but due to the difference in wealth, he felt ashamed to associate with them, so they became estranged. However, he was sure that Qin was Hongkui's concubine. When Hongkui and Qin lived together, he often went to their home. The defendant strongly denied that the obituary submitted by the plaintiff was forged, and he was also aware of this. When Ma Fuqi passed away, the printed obituary included the childhood names of Hongkui's children, such as Baigou and Anan. Later, Wang Jianzhong, a friend of Ma, who was an official in the military headquarters, believed that the position of the Ma family was no longer what it used to be, and it would be embarrassing to include such inelegant childhood names in the obituary. Therefore, he advised the family to reprint it. At that time, the Ma family felt that it was necessary to replace and reprint the obituary. The previous one was destroyed, and the names of Baigou and others were changed to Lusheng and Luying before being published. At this point, the court asked Ma Honggen if he knew Ma Qin and her son. He replied, "I don't know." When asked how the obituary was printed at that time, he replied, "I don't know. I was living abroad at the time." When asked if Ma Qin had come to the funeral, he replied, "I don't know. We were in the mourning hall at the time and could not see them." After legal arguments by both sides, the court announced the conclusion of the trial and scheduled the judgment for the afternoon of the 17th.

Tang Jinbao Used Counterfeit Coins at Fish Stall; Awaiting Investigation

Tang Jinbao from Huzhou went to the Hongkou vegetable market at 7:30 AM on the 1st of this month and used a counterfeit silver yuan to buy fish worth 180文 (wén - copper coins) from Xin Fangcai, a Ningbo fishmonger, asking for change. Xin did not notice at the time and was fooled. Only later did he realize what had happened. The other day at 9:00 AM, Tang went to the same market again, attempting to use counterfeit coins at other vegetable stalls. He was spotted by Xin and handed over to Chinese Constable No. 420. Two identical silver coins were found on him. He was taken to the Hongkou police station and detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to Criminal Division 3 of the First Special Court. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the工部局 (Gōngbùjú - Municipal Council) stated that the defendant claimed at the police station that he got the counterfeit coins from his friend Zeng Fu at the tea house No. 335 Guangfu Road in Zhabei. The police sent detectives to investigate. According to the owner of the tea house, Yun, there was no such person as Zeng Fu and he did not know the defendant. The lawyer believed that this was a lie and asked for an extension to investigate further. The counterfeit coin was presented for inspection. When questioned, the defendant's testimony was evasive. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered him to remain in custody and scheduled a later date for investigation.

Yan Fusun Recruits Direct Disciples

Yan Fusun from Tongxiang is famous for his gourd fortune-telling and has a reputation as 君平 (Jun Ping) reborn. Due to increasing writing work and poor health, he urgently wants to pass on his knowledge and skills. He plans to recruit several direct disciples, regardless of gender or age. They only need to have a basic understanding of Chinese studies and a desire for literature. They can register. After being admitted, they will be taught using correspondence methods. After half a year of training, their achievements will be tested. They may be invited to assist in daily writing work and be paid accordingly, or they may choose to set up their own fortune-telling booths, as they wish. Yan Fusun previously stopped writing due to family mourning but has now resumed his practice. Gourd fortune-telling is open as usual. The usual fee is 4.4 yuan, and the annual fortune is 8.8 yuan. People from other ports can also send letters to request fortune-telling.

The next day, only Dr. Li Meiling's pigeon arrived in Shanghai first. It was just one pigeon. It is said that the pigeon was also the first to arrive during the Jinan race last year. Yangzhong Fellow Villagers Association Prepares for Literacy School

The Yangzhong Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai held an executive committee meeting yesterday. More than 20 people attended, including Dai Zhonghong, Yang Zhengfu, Feng Jingshan, and Zhu Shihuang. Wu Fujun was elected as chairman. After reporting on the purpose of the meeting and the progress of the work, the meeting discussed preparing for a literacy school, raising funds, surveying locations, and reporting to the municipal party headquarters. Preparations will begin immediately. The meeting continued to discuss ways to carry out the association's affairs. Feng Jingshan proposed that team leaders be appointed to solicit members and collect membership fees from old members to re-register and issue membership cards for statistical purposes. Zhu Baohuang proposed that after the re-registration procedures are completed, a long-term school should be established in the area where fellow villagers in Shanghai are most concentrated to facilitate the schooling of fellow villagers' children. Other matters to be handled will be carried out selectively to the extent of the available financial resources. Those executive committee members who abandon their responsibilities and do not attend meetings regularly will be sent letters of advice in order to cooperate fully and gradually realize the unfinished work and meet the expectations of the fellow villagers. The resolution was passed and distributed to all for attention. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Shanghai Tennis Club played against the French Business Association in the grass tennis league at the French Business Association yesterday. The You Team is the strongest in this year's league. The total score was 9 to 6, with the victory going to the French Business Association.

Competition Situation

Qiu Feihai's technology seems to have regressed. The net interception frequently touches the net, and the ball is often out of bounds. The French Business Association's second group, Bai Lunshi and Ke Erqiao, are extraordinarily fierce. The Xu and Chen duo of the Shanghai Club were not their opponents. The fifth group of French Business won three straight, which was also the fatal blow to the Shanghai Club.

Municipal National Arts Hall Sets Up Obligatory Teaching

In order to popularize national arts throughout the city and enhance the health of citizens, the Municipal National Arts Hall has jointly established an obligatory national arts class with the Shanghai Municipal People's Education Center and the Fifth District Tobacco Industry Union in places such as the Women's Temple Park and Pudong, providing completely free teaching. Ministry of Education Supervisor Zhong Inspects and Reports on Vocational Education in Shanxi Province

Supervisor and Section Chief of the Ministry of Education, Zhong Daozan, reported on the vocational education in Shanxi Province as follows: Vocational education in the province has always been very rudimentary. Since the proposal to expand it in the 23rd year (of the Republic), after completely transforming the attached secondary schools of the six normal schools, women's normal schools, national normal schools, and agricultural and industrial specialized schools into vocational schools or departments, there has been gradual improvement. Currently, there are three provincial-level junior agricultural vocational schools in Changzhi, Yuncheng, and Shuoxian; the provincial Yuncheng prison affairs junior vocational school; the provincial Daiyue animal husbandry junior vocational school; and two junior vocational departments of electrification and chemistry attached to the National Normal School. Besides these, there are very few county-run or private vocational schools. Among the aforementioned schools, the three agricultural vocational schools are poorly managed and urgently need improvement. The animal husbandry vocational school is performing relatively well, and the electrification and chemistry departments have very good methods. In recent years, the province has been focusing on economic construction and making every effort. The more than twenty production agencies under the Northwest Industrial Corporation are the driving force behind all of its construction. It should strive for close cooperation between construction and education, basing it on the needs of reality and as a foundation for cultivating talent. Considering the state of vocational education in the province, the following key points should be noted in the future:

1. Provide subsidies to Shanxi students graduating from universities or colleges outside the province to serve as faculty in vocational schools in the province. After graduation, the department should consult with the original school to allow them to stay at the school as assistants or interns in factories or farms, or introduce them to other relevant institutions for one or two years of practice to increase their skills and experience. All expenses should be appropriately provided by the department.

2. The transformation of national normal schools into vocational schools has recently begun to be realized. The first two junior vocational departments of electrical installation and repair and simple chemistry are being established, attached to the Yucai Machine Factory and the Match Factory. All managers and instructors are concurrently factory directors and technicians from each factory. The method is very good. However, the school still has surplus class funds for this year, and next year there will be an additional three class funds. It should make full use of the province's various production institutions to train various mid-level technicians in the Northwest Ten-Year Economic Construction Plan, as needed.

3. The electrification and chemistry departments of the National Normal School currently graduate in two years, focusing on technology and factory experience. If the management is effective, it can be extended for two years to add advanced courses. In the latter two years, attention should be paid to academic theory to seek further study and to improve the industry.

4. After the National Normal School is transformed into various vocational schools, it should unite with the responsible personnel of cooperative organizations to form a teaching, training, and research committee, chaired by the principal, as a guiding mechanism for all facilities. It must eliminate the accumulated malpractices of the old-style apprenticeship system, implement economically effective management methods, and not only adapt to the factory environment and develop work habits as the only purpose.

5. In addition to cooperating as much as possible with the province's original industries and production institutions, the National Normal School should select some departments that are simple to equip and where talent can be recruited according to the needs of the province and run them on campus as appropriate.

6. After the six provincial normal schools are closed, it is proposed to transform them into weaving and dyeing departments, linking them with the spinning mills that are about to open, which is not inappropriate. After the three women's normal schools are closed, the original funds should be used to run complete women's vocational schools, focusing on home economics and other departments. At the same time, special attention should also be paid to the housework and labor of general girls' middle schools and women's normal schools.

7. The provincial junior animal husbandry vocational department is being run at the construction factory's animal husbandry experiment field and has achieved considerable success. However, the time limit is too short and the recurring expenses are also insufficient. In accordance with the regulations, the expenses of other provincial vocational schools should be increased uniformly.

8. The provincial Yuncheng, Shuoxian, and Changzhi junior agricultural vocational schools have been ordered to stop enrolling students due to poor management. After the original students graduate, they will be reorganized, which is not inappropriate. However, preparations should be made early and the content should be enriched to build a good foundation.

9. The leather making and ceramics departments of the industrial college have excellent equipment and should be opened as advanced vocational departments as soon as possible according to the original plan. The apprentice classes and pottery worker classes of the original dyeing and weaving departments should be changed to vocational supplementary classes. The agricultural college should also refer to the industrial college for management.

10. The research on pottery theft in the industrial college over the years has achieved some results, but the style, design, and coloring still need to be improved. The products produced seem to be too thick and the output is too small to meet the needs of society.

11. The private Mingxian Middle School has gold work, wool weaving factories, and a farm, which is rare in general middle schools. Junior high school students must learn all three, two hours per week. Senior high school students choose one of the three, six hours per week, to cultivate vocational interest. This should be advanced to the junior high school stage. In addition to two hours of in-class learning, use spare time to do more work to develop their interest in work. At the same time, investigate their personality, ability, and economic environment, divide them into two groups for further education and non-further education, and use existing equipment to attach appropriate agricultural and industrial vocational departments to train technicians.

12. The arm department of Datong County Industrial Apprentice School should be closed immediately and transformed into a chemical technology department. There are too many Chinese language hours in the shoe making and engraving departments, and the practice time is too short. The two hours of the Three Principles of the People should be changed to one hour of civics. The regulations of vocational supplementary schools should be referred to, with 70% of the time for work and 30% for class. The school name should also be changed to Datong County Industrial Technology Vocational Supplementary School.

13. The province ordered senior elementary schools in each county, or towns and villages planning to run senior elementary schools, to open vocational supplementary schools or classes. The departments should be based on the actual needs of the local area, and it is not appropriate to run commerce first in all cases. 14. Regarding vocational education for local women, a research committee should be convened with the county government to study the supplementary education institutions in each county that have improved women's weaving industry to varying degrees. If necessary, the administration of this project will be entirely managed by the department.

Although the graduates of this year's mining, metallurgy, mechanical engineering, and other departments have not yet finished their exams, they have all been hired. Cultural Buildings in the Central District of the City: Library and Museum to be Completed on Schedule: Construction Project Nearly Completed, to be Completed in August: Chairman Ye Gongchuo Discusses Recurring Expenses

The five major buildings being constructed by the municipal government in the central district of the city are progressing rapidly. The municipal library and museum, which are related to culture, will be completed by the end of August. The temporary board of directors is working on the equipment and funding for the two buildings. The reporter met with Ye Gongwei, the chairman of the museum board, yesterday and learned the details from the municipal government as follows:

Library: The municipal library started construction in September last year and held a foundation laying ceremony on December 1st. The project is progressing rapidly. The first layer of steel-reinforced concrete was completed in mid-March, and the second layer is now more than half completed. It is expected to be fully completed before the end of August. Most of the building is two stories high, with an average exterior wall height of about 12 meters. A large platform is planned in front of the main entrance, with flagpoles erected on both sides of the platform to enhance the view. Regarding equipment, a temporary board of directors has been established, and Cai Yuanpei has been invited as the temporary chairman. The planning, equipment, and layout are currently underway.

Museum: The municipal museum is located between the left and right sides of the government front road, facing west to the east, opposite the library. The exterior of the museum is similar to that of the library. The entire building is a steel-reinforced concrete fireproof structure. The exterior walls are built with artificial stone, and the project is progressing in the same way as the library. It is expected to be completed by the end of August. Regarding the equipment and recurring expense budget, the temporary chairman of the museum was interviewed yesterday. It is currently being actively prepared. The expense budget has been sent to the Executive Yuan for approval, and the details will be announced after this.

Changtai County, Fujian Province Inspection Group: Returns to Xiamen After Inspecting Education in Various Provinces

Changtai County, Fujian Province, has a population of only over 80,000, but its primary education is very developed. In mid-April, the Education Research Association initiated a new education visit group to various provinces, consisting of 15 people, all principals of private schools in the county. On the 5th of this month, they departed from Zhangzhou, passing through Xiamen, Shanghai, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Wuxi, Nanjing, Jinan, Tianjin, and Peiping, visiting famous elementary schools and social education institutions. Yesterday, they returned to Shanghai from Peiping and stayed at Datong. In recent days, they have observed the popular education methods of the Shanghai Agricultural Studies Group, the Nian Style Society, and the Industrial Studies Group for Little Teachers, believing that they are the most suitable for poor rural areas. They plan to take the Taikoo liner back to Fujian today.
