Lamp (Part Two)

— Tan Tan

In the previous article, I wrote a little about my miscellaneous affairs with lamps. Below I will write more about the knowledge of lamps.

In ancient times, there was probably only fire and no lamps. What is called "Chai" in the Book of Documents is not necessary to say? That is, when Liu Xiang checked the books, Tian Lu (?): with a brush made with the fire of artemisia as the lamp, climbing into the clouds, it was only fire and not lamps. In the Biography of Chen Sheng and Wu Guang in the Records of the Grand Historian, "Chou Huo Hu Ming", although "Chou Huo" is also called "Chou Deng" by later generations, it is only a later type of lantern. I don't know which came first, candles or oil lamps. Even taking "burning the belly to be a lamp" as an example, I don't know if their "lamp" knew that oil could be used to light a lamp first. Later, seeing that the dead were fat, their stomachs must have a lot of oil, so they used them as lamps?

According to the theory, then oil lamps came before candles; because the completion of candles clearly knows that oil can light a lamp, and then condenses it to make a candle. But opening the ancient books, it clearly says that candles are mentioned more than lamps, and earlier than lamps. If you say that lamps are more aristocratic and used by fewer people, then solitary lamps and green lamps are clearly very shabby, while red candles and magnificent candles are so rich?

In the Book of Songs, "The torches in the courtyard began to shine", the torches used charcoal, not oil. When Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty watched the ghost of Lady Li at night, I don't know if it was under the light of a lamp or under the light of a candle?

In Li Shangyin's poem, "Pearl floats, floating lamp returns alone", I don't know whether it uses candles or oil, meaning that the thing you hold while walking is mostly candles like the later lanterns and gauze lamps. "When should we cut the candles at the west window together!" "The wax torch turns to ashes, the tears begin to dry", in the Tang Dynasty, candles were probably more common. And "at dusk, the Han Palace passes candles", "painting short, suffering the night is long, why must you hold a candle to tour", at the end of the Dynasty, during the Eastern Han Dynasty, candles were undoubtedly already used.

Buddhist temples have lamps that are long-burning lamps, which use oil. Buddhism was introduced into China during the Eastern Han Dynasty. I don't know when the long-burning lamps were lit. Did they exist as soon as they were brought from India?

Lamps and candles are probably used interchangeably. Even if a candle is used, as long as a cover or something is added to the candle, people will also call it a lamp. It seems that gauze lamps and lanterns do not use candles, but it does not prevent them from being called lamps.

In the past, during the prosperous times, flower lanterns were often released on the night of the Lantern Festival, expressing the idea of ​​singing and dancing in peace. Especially the people of Jiangnan are accustomed to ingenuity, so the spring lamps in Wu and Yue and other places are unusually detailed. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, King Fu occupied Jiangnan. At that time, Qing soldiers were already approaching Jinling City, but the old gentleman was still in a leisurely mood and greatly appreciated the spring lamps in Nanjing City. "I heard that the city is full of artillery fire, and the deep palace is still appreciating spring lamps", this matter is forever lamented by historians. In fact, with this lamp story in history, the value of the lamp immediately increased a lot. Although its merit and power are in some places completely the same as the sun.

Naturally, modern cities are even more indispensable to lamps. If Shanghai has no lamps, there will be no Shanghai at night, and if there is no Shanghai at night, there will be no Shanghai.

Haters of material civilization hate everything new. In fact, this only shows their ignorance. Taking lamps as an example, the beautiful colors of the neon lamps beautify the city, let alone that, even ordinary electric lights will immediately bring you from the real world to a misty dreamland as long as you add a beautiful tassel cover on all four sides. "Ten thousand people under the lamp", it helps people to be charming, doesn't it?

"The moon sets, the birds cry, the frost fills the sky, the maple leaves are against the fishing fire, sleep with melancholy", "The tide falls, the night river is in the oblique moon, two or three points of fire are Guazhou", naturally, what I miss most is not the red lights of the city, not the silver candles in the halls, but a few fishing lights in the empty water of the river. But I haven't seen them for a long time?

Garden and Forest

— Hua Mu

In summer, gardens and forests are lush and dense, with branches and leaves laden with fruit, constantly tempting passersby with umbrellas outside the garden. The wind carries the blazing heat of the midday sun through the shade of the trees. From time to time, a few clear bird calls scatter from the branches and leaves: the cicadas, as if unable to endure the sun's scorching heat, lie under the leaves, stretching their voices to the limit to drink. Longans are almost ripe and sweet, and children often sneak in from the garden walls to steal them, so someone has to guard them there: the guard is the grandfather, who sits under a green shade every afternoon, always waving a large cattail fan in his hand, lying on a bamboo chair, looking at the fruits on the branches, a smile on his face: the long beard, draped over his chest, occasionally sways gently with the fanning wind.

In the garden, there are more than twenty longan and pomelo trees in total, all planted by the grandfather himself, and there is also a lychee tree, squeezed between a longan and a pomelo tree, which the grandfather cherishes the most. After several years of hard work, the longan and pomelo trees began to bear a lot of fruit that year, and the grandfather was naturally very proud. At that time, I was about six years old. The sixth and seventh months of the lunar calendar in my hometown were the busy farming season, and the mothers had little time at home during the day, so I had to follow my grandfather with my older sister, and my grandfather certainly loved his grandchildren. The children in the countryside are naturally more wild, and although my sister was only two years older than me, she had already learned how to climb trees. Often, when my grandfather was taking a nap, my sister would use the excuse of catching cicadas to climb up the tree and pick some longans, and the two of us would share them behind my grandfather's back: the longans were not yet fully ripe. Although they tasted astringent, they still felt sweet and delicious. But every time, my grandfather would find out, and we would inevitably be scolded. However, my grandfather always loved us very much, and he would let us make trouble afterwards. Once, just after a heavy rain, the branches were slippery, and I encouraged my sister to climb the tree again. Unfortunately, this time it caused a disaster. My sister fell down, lying on the ground with blood flowing from her mouth. Although we unexpectedly got a handful of longans, my sister's two front teeth were broken.

By the beginning of July, most of the longans were gradually ripe and sweet. At this time, my grandfather no longer forbade us, and he would always pick a basket every day and share some with me and my sister. Children's desires are never satisfied, and when my grandfather wasn't paying attention, we still went to steal some. Because it was the first year of fruiting, the amount of fruit was limited, and it wasn't prepared to be picked and sold, but rather left on the trees to wait for the aunts to come back. The most interesting of the aunts were the second aunts, Wan and Mei. When the two of them were together, they always made a lot of jokes. Aunt Wan was famous for eating fruit, not afraid of sour or astringent, ripe or unripe, she ate them all with relish. As soon as Aunt Wan came, even the pomelos that were still far from ripe had to be picked a few. At that time, we always looked forward to our aunts coming back, so we could eat and eat a lot and make trouble with our aunts. My sister could also volunteer to climb the tree, and my grandfather wouldn't stop her anymore. My grandfather didn't like to eat longans (and didn't seem to eat other fruits much either), but when he saw us gathered under the tree eating wildly, he laughed happily.

That year, the garden was the most beautiful and lovely in my childhood life.

Now, my grandfather has long since passed away, and his tombstone has even turned brown: my own feet have stepped onto the road of life, bearing some tangible and intangible responsibilities as a person: my sister, too, has become the mother of two children: my aunts have changed even more quickly, not to mention the second aunts Wan and Mei, and the family of Aunt Kai, who was always considered well-off, has also declined in recent years. Although the garden is still there, and the longan and pomelo trees still bloom and bear fruit every year, the beautiful and lovely scene of happiness and joy from those days can never be woven back into the garden!

It is said that the lychee tree that my grandfather particularly cherished has never borne fruit even once until now. I think that if my grandfather knew about this in the afterlife, it would probably be something he wouldn't be happy about?

Alas, the garden in my memory, the dream of a happy childhood in the past, is now gone, gone.

Sickness

— Hua Zhi

I've been sick for over a month recently. It started with a headache. Of course, I didn't consider that the beginning of an illness. I took a dose of Tiger Head brand headache powder and continued to work as usual without paying attention. The next day, I developed a fever. The corners of my temples felt like they were on fire, and my palms and soles of my feet were also burning hot. This was definitely a sign of illness. I went home, boiled a dose of midday tea, and covered myself with a quilt to sleep. This was what my grandmother always reminded me to do as if it were a big deal. As long as I broke out in a sweat at night, the illness would suddenly disappear. When I woke up in the middle of the night, my body felt as if it had been dragged out of water. The next morning, I went back to work as usual, although I still felt dizzy and lightheaded, and I walked a bit unsteadily. It was the season of yellow plums. It is said that Southerners value "dampness." It was the time of damp toxins, and everyone had this phenomenon. In fact, the illness had officially begun. Three days later, my legs could no longer support my body from the bed.

Illness must be treated. The lives of poor people are sometimes perhaps more precious than those of the rich. With the help of my family, I went to a nearby hospital. The doctor, besides knowing that my pulse was higher than normal, said it was heat and gave me several colors of white medicine powder, with the words "take three times a day after meals" written on the paper package. This kind of diagnosis was probably the most thorough it could be.

I finished the six packets of medicine powder in two days, and I felt the same as before taking the medicine. My wife secretly invited a doctor for me. After a thorough examination, he came to the same conclusion: it was the flu. He wrote a prescription and instructed me to rest quietly. The cost was more than twenty times the hospital's registration fee, not including the cost of the medicine.

But perhaps the expensive doctor couldn't cure the poor man's illness. His medicine worsened my condition. I slept dazedly all day long, my body scorched by a high fever, but when it was time to light the lamps, I would wake up as if I were a normal person, and then I couldn't sleep until dawn. This situation lasted for a week. I changed three doctors, and my illness seemed to have become incurable. I could tell from their repeated head-shaking. When I was a child, I had the same kind of serious illness. I only knew that a strange doctor came to check my pulse every day, sometimes even two or three. The room was crowded with neighbors and relatives. Their whispers often made me angry for no reason. My mother stayed by my bedside all day long, with tears in her eyes, as if someone was going to take me away. But I was completely blank, and when I woke up, I would think of many things I wanted to eat, and it was best to get them right away, even things like cigarettes that I had never put in my mouth before. This made the people who visited me anxious. They thought it was delirium. A twelve or thirteen-year-old child could never think of so many items. But when they were discussing it quietly, I could hear them clearly. This abnormal hearing also made them suspicious. Later, I learned that my illness lasted for a year. Not a single licensed doctor was willing to come, and in the end, no one could diagnose the correct disease. This was very much in line with my personality. I often deliberately made people not understand me, even my closest friends. But this time I got sick, I completely changed my ways. I hoped that a doctor would cure my illness immediately, or even kill me with a dose of the opposite medicine. Because I was no longer a twelve or thirteen-year-old child, and my mother was no longer there to take care of me. Although my wife had taken my mother's place, those people who I used to hate for whispering were nowhere to be seen. Being able to change three doctors, my wife had probably exhausted her last resources. The world of the past and my mother's death were buried at the same time. In this month-long illness, I learned the secret of how to live in the present society. Although I always hoped to get out of bed, it was never a bad thing to gain a little more life experience. Thinking like this, my illness got better as it followed its natural course.

Sisters-in-Law (Part 1)

— Ling Zixi

It hasn't been long since Zhang Gen died, but since the end of the seventh-day memorial, his family has been arguing and fighting every two or three days. Even the neighbors on the left and right went from talking about it to disliking it, from disliking it to hating it, and later on, it was even a little alarming - constantly arguing from early in the morning until late at night; fighting, scolding, crying and shouting. They were also making trouble by hanging themselves or jumping into the river to commit suicide. The noise made people feel uneasy, and they themselves were only concerned with arguing and scheming, trying to gain a little secret advantage and verbal "glory." Like this, who wouldn't hate it, who wouldn't hope for a little peace?

However, Zhang Gen's family was still making trouble "every two or three days."

As a result, the people in the village often made the two "quarrelers" in Zhang Gen's family the object of their comments and the source of their idle talk in the morning and evening.

"They're arguing like enemies, when will it ever stop?"

"Stop? You don't understand at all! When Zhang Gen's wife came through the door, the Taoist Wang in the town secretly said to people: Zhang Gen's mother and sister are both born in the year of the Tiger, and the bride is born in the year of the Sheep. A sheep entering a tiger's mouth will suffer."

"That's right! A sheep entering a tiger's mouth, their fates are incompatible. Don't you know?"

"But I say, Zhang Gen's mother has lived a long time. How can she not understand a little! It's common for a daughter-in-law and a sister-in-law not to get along. But the mother-in-law doesn't try to reconcile them. Instead, she adds fuel to the fire, joining her daughter in tormenting the widowed daughter-in-law. Every day, from early in the morning, she complains and curses. Is that how things should be done?"

"Their fates are incompatible - after all, the daughter is family, blood relatives, think about it, who wouldn't help their own family, who wouldn't help their daughter instead of the widowed daughter-in-law?"

Broadcasting News

The So-and-So Singing Society, established for half a year, has been praised by all sectors of society. Now, in order to expand its scope, it is seeking singing talents. Any ladies who love singing, have good conduct, and no bad habits are welcome to join. A small allowance will be given. Please send a letter to Mr. Xu Wuyi, c/o Zhongjiafu Gift Shop, Hankou Road. The society aims to promote elegant music and singing and to promote art. It currently broadcasts on a major radio station every evening.

The Nature Orchestra has gained a reputation since broadcasting new songs on various radio stations. Now, due to internal expansion, it plans to recruit male and female members. Those with a certain level of education and some understanding of music theory can contact Mr. Li Gongxia at the Industrial Bureau Library, 22 Nanjing Road, from 12:00 PM to 2:00 PM every Wednesday and Saturday.

Movie News

Yi Hua Special Report

Yuan Meiyun received a letter yesterday from someone who signed his name as Zheng Jiazhen. The letter contained the following sentences: "...The other day I went to Jincheng to see "The Beginning of Man," and I thought the part where you and Wang Yin got married and entered the bridal chamber was very beautiful, especially when the wedding hostess whispered in your ear, your shy performance was really good, but I don't know what the wedding hostess said to you? Miss: Tomorrow is Sunday again, and I still want to go to Jincheng to see your masterpiece "The Beginning of Man" again...". After reading the letter, Meiyun said, "Oh my god! How am I supposed to reply to this letter?

Fatty Guan Hongda plays a foolish farmer in Bu Wancang's "Triumphant Song". Yesterday, when he performed, the audience laughed at his funny performance.

Yuan Congmei said confidently... "No matter what, "Storm" is a step forward compared to "Iron Crow"." Judging by Lao Yuan's confidence, I think "Storm" is indeed worthy of our attention.

Wan Laitian plays A Gui in "Hero of the Hour," and the newcomer Zhang Wen plays his sister.

"Hero of the Hour" features figures in Qing Dynasty clothing, strange and unusual.

Shi Dongshan's new work after "The Beginning of Man" is being written.

Lianhua Tidbits

The interlude of "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp" is called "You Are My Lifeline". The score is by the talented musician Mr. Ma Sicong. This song is already popular in Lianhua.

Sun Yu's new sound film "Go to Nature" is extremely satirical. It can be said that it will open up a new path for national films in terms of material. Outdoor scenes are planned to be filmed in Qingdao.

Fei Mu called Wu Yonggang a genius because his thinking is sharp and profound. Wu is a prolific writer, and he has written four or five scripts since "Little Angel". The selected script is called "Waves Washing Sand" and is planned to star Jin Yan.

Zhu Shilin's new work after "National Style" is a social ethics drama.

Wang Cilong will begin directing "Dayuling". The scriptwriter is Mr. Liang Desuo.

The protagonist of "Little Angel," Wang Renmei, said to Bai Lu, "My dog is called Lulu!" Bai Lu rolled her eyes.

The eldest sister of the Liang family, Sai Zhen, performed deeply and movingly in "Four Sisters," which is completely different from her style in "Femme Fatale." The two scenes of her father's death and her sister's escape are touching and tearful.

Yang Maotou, the little girl who sells newspapers on Avenue Joffre, is Lianhua's special contract actor. She will appear on the screen in Ma Xubang's "Rain of Pear Blossoms" and will also appear in Ma Xu's new work "Wild Geese Descending on Cold River" - playing Chen Yanyan's sister.

The Two Railway Bureaus Compile and Print "Southeast Pagoda Shadows"

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, in order to promote the scenic spots of Jiangsu and Zhejiang and increase the interest of Chinese people in tourism, in addition to successively printing guidebooks to various places along the line and selling them at low prices, have recently collected 38 famous pagoda shadows in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, accompanied by a brief history of the pagodas and an overview of the surrounding scenery, and compiled them into a book called "Southeast Pagoda Shadows". The book is rich in pictures and texts and full of charm. The entire book is 60 pages long, exquisitely printed on rough rice-colored copperplate paper, and sells for two dimes per copy. Sales locations include: various stations and business offices of the railway, Shanghai Simalu Life Bookstore, Shanghai Sichuan Road China Travel Service headquarters and branches.

McCagle Wind Broadcast

Shen Xiling's fully dubbed new sound film "Nostalgia" was secretly screened at the Central Grand Theater last Saturday night at 11:30 PM with excellent results.

Beiping Xinyi Company plans to build a brand new cinema at the west entrance of Xizongbu Hutong and is currently bidding for preparations.

Zhang Shichuan's "Big Family," directed by one person with the entire cast, has been working hard these two days. The scene in a grand ancient hall yesterday at Yucheng Studio was extremely grand and lasted from 7:00 PM until the next morning.

Mr. Wu Xueyun, an employee of the Mingxing Company, was recently hired by the Northwest Film Company. Yesterday, more than a dozen colleagues and friends from the press held a public banquet at Yunji Sichuan Restaurant on Yier Malu.

It is said that the registration for the Film Talents Teaching Institute, the third step of the Chinese Film Society's work, will begin on the 15th. The quota is 100 men and women in total. The prospectus will be sent by mail upon request.

It is said that the fifth issue of Mingxing Biweekly contains Xiao Ying's "My Dancing Experience" and Wu Cun's "Moving Story," which are quite funny. There is also Wang Huijuan's reply to Tang Yu, but the content is unknown.

The Sports World, published every Saturday, also has film articles and news. Its supplement is called "Screen and Stage" and is edited by Dongsheng.

"Jealousy" is Released

This is a film produced by Columbia Pictures in the United States, which tells the story of a boxer who becomes jealous of his lover's association with other men, resulting in a bloody tragedy. However, it turns out to be a dream. The plot is very deep and tense. It stars the three major stars, Sweetheart Nancy Carroll, Donald Cook, and George M. P. Barr. It is currently being shown in Nanjing.
